		<div id="mw-indicator-pp-default" class="mw-indicator"><div class="mw-parser-output"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Protection_policy#semi" title="This article is semi-protected."><img alt="Page semi-protected" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1b/Semi-protection-shackle.svg/20px-Semi-protection-shackle.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="20" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1b/Semi-protection-shackle.svg/30px-Semi-protection-shackle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1b/Semi-protection-shackle.svg/40px-Semi-protection-shackle.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="512" /></a></span></div></div>
		</div>

						<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
					</div>
					<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-content-subtitle"></div></div>
					
					
					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Conspiracy theories regarding the September 11 attacks</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:World_Trade_Center,_New_York_City_-_aerial_view_(March_2001).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/World_Trade_Center%2C_New_York_City_-_aerial_view_%28March_2001%29.jpg/220px-World_Trade_Center%2C_New_York_City_-_aerial_view_%28March_2001%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="311" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/World_Trade_Center%2C_New_York_City_-_aerial_view_%28March_2001%29.jpg/330px-World_Trade_Center%2C_New_York_City_-_aerial_view_%28March_2001%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/World_Trade_Center%2C_New_York_City_-_aerial_view_%28March_2001%29.jpg/440px-World_Trade_Center%2C_New_York_City_-_aerial_view_%28March_2001%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1361" data-file-height="1924" /></a><figcaption>The nature of <a href="/wiki/Collapse_of_the_World_Trade_Center" title="Collapse of the World Trade Center">the collapse</a> of the two <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_(1973%E2%80%932001)" title="World Trade Center (1973\xe2\x80\x932001)">World Trade Center</a> towers and the nearby <a href="/wiki/7_World_Trade_Center" title="7 World Trade Center">7 World Trade Center</a> (in this photo, the brown building to the left of the towers) is a major focus of <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">9/11</a> conspiracy theories.</figcaption></figure>
<p>There are various <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theory" title="Conspiracy theory">conspiracy theories</a> that attribute the preparation and execution of the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> against the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> to parties other than, or in addition to, <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Norman_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norman-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> These include the theory that high-level government officials had <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks_advance-knowledge_conspiracy_theories" title="September 11 attacks advance-knowledge conspiracy theories">advance knowledge of the attacks</a>. Government investigations and independent reviews have rejected these theories.<sup id="cite_ref-popularmechanics.com_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popularmechanics.com-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Purdue_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Purdue-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Proponents of these theories assert that there are inconsistencies in the commonly accepted version, or that there exists evidence that was ignored, concealed, or overlooked.<sup id="cite_ref-VF_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VF-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The most prominent conspiracy theory is that the <a href="/wiki/Collapse_of_the_World_Trade_Center" title="Collapse of the World Trade Center">collapse of the Twin Towers</a> and <a href="/wiki/7_World_Trade_Center" title="7 World Trade Center">7 World Trade Center</a> were the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_controlled_demolition_conspiracy_theories" title="World Trade Center controlled demolition conspiracy theories">result of controlled demolitions</a> rather than structural failure due to impact and fire.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Another prominent belief is that <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">the Pentagon</a> was hit by a missile launched by elements from inside the U.S. government,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-usgovDidPlaneHitPentagon_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usgovDidPlaneHitPentagon-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> or that hijacked planes were remotely controlled, or that a commercial airliner was allowed to do so via an effective stand-down of the American military. Possible motives claimed by conspiracy theorists for such actions include justifying the invasions of <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%932021)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001\xe2\x80\x932021)">Afghanistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq</a> (even though the U.S. government concluded Iraq was not involved in the attacks)<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> to advance their <a href="/wiki/Geostrategy" title="Geostrategy">geostrategic</a> interests, such as <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan%E2%80%93Afghanistan%E2%80%93Pakistan%E2%80%93India_Pipeline" title="Turkmenistan\xe2\x80\x93Afghanistan\xe2\x80\x93Pakistan\xe2\x80\x93India Pipeline">plans to construct a natural gas pipeline through Afghanistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Knight_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Other conspiracy theories revolve around authorities having advance knowledge of the attacks and deliberately ignoring or assisting the attackers.<sup id="cite_ref-VF_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VF-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Eleventh_Day_pp92_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Eleventh_Day_pp92-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCevolution_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCevolution-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Standards_and_Technology" title="National Institute of Standards and Technology">National Institute of Standards and Technology</a> (NIST) and the technology magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Popular_Mechanics" title="Popular Mechanics">Popular Mechanics</a></i> have investigated and rejected the claims made by 9/11 conspiracy theorists.<sup id="cite_ref-investigation_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investigation-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-finalreport_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finalreport-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PopMech-ConspiracyIndustry-2006_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopMech-ConspiracyIndustry-2006-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/9/11_Commission" title="9/11 Commission">9/11 Commission</a> and most of the <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">civil engineering</a> community accept that the impacts of jet aircraft at high speeds in combination with subsequent fires, not controlled demolition, led to the collapse of the Twin Towers,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> but some conspiracy theory groups, including <a href="/wiki/Architects_%26_Engineers_for_9/11_Truth" title="Architects &amp; Engineers for 9/11 Truth">Architects &amp; Engineers for 9/11 Truth</a>, disagree with the arguments made by NIST and <i>Popular Mechanics</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KGO_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KGO-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span></h2>
<p>9/11 conspiracy theorists reject one or both of the following facts about the 9/11 attacks:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">Al-Qaeda</a> suicide operatives hijacked and crashed <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines_Flight_175" title="United Airlines Flight 175">United Airlines Flight 175</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines_Flight_11" title="American Airlines Flight 11">American Airlines Flight 11</a> into the twin towers of the World Trade Center, and crashed <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines_Flight_77" title="American Airlines Flight 77">American Airlines Flight 77</a> into the Pentagon. The impact and resulting fires caused the collapse of the Twin Towers and the destruction and damage of other buildings in the World Trade Center complex. The Pentagon was severely damaged by the impact of the airliner and the resulting fire. The hijackers also crashed <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines_Flight_93" title="United Airlines Flight 93">a fourth plane</a> into a field near <a href="/wiki/Shanksville,_Pennsylvania" title="Shanksville, Pennsylvania">Shanksville, Pennsylvania</a> after the passengers and flight crew attempted to regain control of the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Pre-attack warnings of varying detail of the planned attacks against the United States by al-Qaeda were ignored due to a lack of communication between various law enforcement and intelligence personnel. For the lack of interagency communication, the 9/11 report cited bureaucratic inertia and laws passed in the 1970s to prevent abuses that caused scandals during that era, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Watergate_scandal" title="Watergate scandal">Watergate scandal</a>. The report faulted both the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Bill_Clinton" title="Presidency of Bill Clinton">Clinton</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_George_W._Bush" title="Presidency of George W. Bush">Bush</a> administrations with "<a href="/wiki/Failure_of_imagination" title="Failure of imagination">failure of imagination</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Schmitt_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmitt-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>This consensus view is backed by various sources, including:
</p>
<ul><li>The reports from government investigations&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 the <a href="/wiki/9/11_Commission_Report" title="9/11 Commission Report">9/11 Commission Report</a> (that incorporated intelligence information from the earlier <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> investigation (<a href="/wiki/PENTTBOM" title="PENTTBOM">PENTTBOM</a>) and the Joint Inquiry of 2002), and the studies into building performance carried out by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Emergency_Management_Agency" title="Federal Emergency Management Agency">Federal Emergency Management Agency</a> (FEMA)<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Standards_and_Technology" title="National Institute of Standards and Technology">National Institute of Standards and Technology</a> (NIST)<sup id="cite_ref-investigation_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investigation-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Investigations by non-government organizations that support the accepted account&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 such as those by scientists at <a href="/wiki/Purdue_University" title="Purdue University">Purdue University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Purdue_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Purdue-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Articles supporting these facts and theories appearing in magazines such as <i><a href="/wiki/Popular_Mechanics" title="Popular Mechanics">Popular Mechanics</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Scientific_American" title="Scientific American">Scientific American</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-PopMech-ConspiracyIndustry-2006_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopMech-ConspiracyIndustry-2006-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Similar articles in news media throughout the world, including <i><a href="/wiki/Times_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Times of India">The Times of India</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Canadian Broadcasting Corporation">Canadian Broadcasting Corporation</a> (CBC),<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Welle" title="Deutsche Welle">Deutsche Welle</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Australian Broadcasting Corporation">Australian Broadcasting Corporation</a> (ABC),<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Chosun_Ilbo" title="The Chosun Ilbo">The Chosun Ilbo</a></i> of South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<p>Since the attacks, a variety of conspiracy theories have been put forward in websites, books and films. Many groups and individuals advocating 9/11 conspiracy theories identify as part of the <a href="/wiki/9/11_Truth_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11 Truth movement">9/11 Truth movement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Within six hours of the attack, a suggestion appeared on an Internet chat room suggesting that the collapse of the towers looked like an act of controlled demolition. "If, in a few days, not one official has mentioned anything about the controlled demolition part," the author wrote, "I think we have a REALLY serious problem."<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The first theories that emerged focused primarily on various perceived anomalies in the publicly available evidence, and proponents later developed more specific theories about an alleged plot.<sup id="cite_ref-Knight_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> One false allegation that was widely circulated by e-mail and on the Web is that not a single Jew had been killed in the attack and that therefore the attacks must have been the work of the <a href="/wiki/Mossad" title="Mossad">Mossad</a>, not Islamic terrorists.<sup id="cite_ref-Knight_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first elaborated theories appeared in Europe. One week after the attacks, the "inside job" theory was the subject of a thesis by a researcher from the <a href="/wiki/French_National_Centre_for_Scientific_Research" title="French National Centre for Scientific Research">French National Centre for Scientific Research</a> published in <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a></i>. Other theories sprang from the far corners of the globe within weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Six months after the attacks, <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Meyssan" title="Thierry Meyssan">Thierry Meyssan</a>\'s piece on 9/11, <i>L\'Effroyable Imposture</i>, topped the French bestseller list. Its publication in English (as <i><a href="/wiki/9/11:_The_Big_Lie" title="9/11: The Big Lie">9/11: The Big Lie</a></i>) received little attention, but it remains one of the principal sources for "trutherism".<sup id="cite_ref-WeeklyStandard_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WeeklyStandard-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> 2003 saw the publication of <i><a href="/wiki/The_CIA_and_September_11_(book)" class="mw-redirect" title="The CIA and September 11 (book)">The CIA and September 11</a></i> by former German state minister <a href="/wiki/Andreas_von_B%C3%BClow" title="Andreas von B\xc3\xbclow">Andreas von B\xc3\xbclow</a> and <i>Operation 9/11</i> by the German journalist Gerhard Wisnewski; both books are published by <a href="/wiki/Mathias_Br%C3%B6ckers" title="Mathias Br\xc3\xb6ckers">Mathias Br\xc3\xb6ckers</a>, who was at the time an editor at the German newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Tageszeitung" title="Die Tageszeitung">Die Tageszeitung</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Knight_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While these theories were popular in Europe, they were treated by the U.S. media with either bafflement or amusement, and they were dismissed by the U.S. government as the product of <a href="/wiki/Anti-Americanism" title="Anti-Americanism">anti-Americanism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Knight-Popular_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight-Popular-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In an address to the United Nations on November 10, 2001, President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> denounced the emergence of "outrageous conspiracy theories&#160;[...] that attempt to shift the blame away from the terrorists, themselves, away from the guilty."<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 9/11 conspiracy theories started out mostly in the political left but have broadened into what <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> magazine describes as "<a href="/wiki/Terra_incognita" title="Terra incognita">terra incognita</a> where left and right meet, fusing <a href="/wiki/Counterculture_of_the_1960s" title="Counterculture of the 1960s">sixties countercultural</a> distrust with the <a href="/wiki/Gadsden_flag" title="Gadsden flag">don\'t-tread-on-me</a> variety".<sup id="cite_ref-StrangeMan_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StrangeMan-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 2004, conspiracy theories about the September 11 attacks began to gain ground in the United States. One explanation is that the rise in popularity stemmed more from growing criticism of the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a> and the newly re-elected President George W. Bush than from any discovery of new or more compelling evidence or an improvement in the technical quality of the presentation of the theories.<sup id="cite_ref-Knight_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Knight_Ridder" title="Knight Ridder">Knight Ridder news</a> theorized that revelations that <a href="/wiki/Weapons_of_mass_destruction" class="mw-redirect" title="Weapons of mass destruction">weapons of mass destruction</a> did not exist in Iraq, the belated release of the <a href="/wiki/President%27s_Daily_Brief_of_August_6,_2001" class="mw-redirect" title="President&#39;s Daily Brief of August 6, 2001">President\'s Daily Brief of August 6, 2001</a>, and reports that <a href="/wiki/NORAD" title="NORAD">NORAD</a> had lied to the <a href="/wiki/9/11_Commission" title="9/11 Commission">9/11 Commission</a>, may have fueled the conspiracy theories.<sup id="cite_ref-Knight_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Between 2004 and the fifth anniversary of the September 11 attacks in 2006, mainstream coverage of the conspiracy theories increased.<sup id="cite_ref-Knight_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The U.S. government issued a formal analysis by the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Standards_and_Technology" title="National Institute of Standards and Technology">National Institute of Standards and Technology</a> (NIST) of the collapse of the World Trade Center.<sup id="cite_ref-nistfaq_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nistfaq-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> To address the growing publicity of the theories, the <a href="/wiki/State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="State Department">State Department</a> revised a webpage in 2006 to debunk them.<sup id="cite_ref-usgovTopConspiracyTheories_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usgovTopConspiracyTheories-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> A 2006 national security strategy paper declared that terrorism springs from "subcultures of conspiracy and misinformation," and that "terrorists recruit more effectively from populations whose information about the world is contaminated by falsehoods and corrupted by conspiracy theories. The distortions keep alive grievances and filter out facts that would challenge popular prejudices and self-serving propaganda."<sup id="cite_ref-NSec2006_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSec2006-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Al-Qaeda has repeatedly claimed responsibility for the attacks, with chief deputy <a href="/wiki/Ayman_al-Zawahiri" title="Ayman al-Zawahiri">Ayman al-Zawahiri</a> accusing <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shia</a> Iran and <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a> of denigrating <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a> successes in hurting America by intentionally starting rumors that Israel carried out the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some of the conspiracy theories about the September 11 attacks do not involve representational strategies typical of many conspiracy theories that establish a clear dichotomy between good and evil, or guilty and innocent; instead, they call up gradations of negligence and complicity. Matthias Br\xc3\xb6ckers, an early proponent of such theories, dismisses the commonly accepted account of the September 11 attacks as being itself a conspiracy theory that seeks "to reduce complexity, disentangle what is confusing," and "explain the inexplicable".<sup id="cite_ref-Knight_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Just before the fifth anniversary of the attacks, mainstream news outlets released a flurry of articles on the growth of 9/11 conspiracy theories,<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> with an article in <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)"><i>Time</i></a> stating that "[t]his is not a fringe phenomenon. It is a mainstream political reality."<sup id="cite_ref-The_Eleventh_Day_pp92_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Eleventh_Day_pp92-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-time_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Several <a href="/wiki/Opinion_polls_about_9/11_conspiracy_theories" title="Opinion polls about 9/11 conspiracy theories">surveys</a> have included questions about beliefs related to the September 11 attacks. In 2008, 9/11 conspiracy theories topped a "greatest conspiracy theory" list compiled by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i>. The list was ranked by following and traction.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, the "International Center for 9/11 Studies," a private organization that is said to be sympathetic to conspiracy theories,<sup id="cite_ref-Bild_Videos_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bild_Videos-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> successfully sued for the release of videos collected by NIST of the attacks and aftermath.<sup id="cite_ref-FAZ_Videos_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAZ_Videos-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NZZ_Nahaufnahme_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NZZ_Nahaufnahme-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> According to the German daily <i><a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Allgemeine_Zeitung" title="Frankfurter Allgemeine Zeitung">Frankfurter Allgemeine Zeitung</a></i>, the videos that were published shortly before the ninth anniversary of the attacks provide "new food for conspiracy theorists." Many of the videos show images of <a href="/wiki/7_World_Trade_Center" title="7 World Trade Center">7 World Trade Center</a>, a skyscraper in the vicinity of the WTC towers that also <a href="/wiki/Collapse_of_the_World_Trade_Center#Collapse_of_7_World_Trade_Center" title="Collapse of the World Trade Center">collapsed</a> on September 11, 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-FAZ_Videos_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAZ_Videos-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>9/11 truth figures <a href="/wiki/Steven_E._Jones" title="Steven E. Jones">Steven E. Jones</a> and Mike Berger have further added that the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Osama_bin_Laden" class="mw-redirect" title="Death of Osama bin Laden">death of Osama bin Laden</a><sup id="cite_ref-binladendeathcelebration_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-binladendeathcelebration-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> did not change their questions about the attacks, nor provide closure.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to writer Jeremy Stahl, since Bush left office, the overall number of believers in 9/11 conspiracy theories has dipped, while the number of people who believe in the most "radical" theories has held fairly steady.<sup id="cite_ref-Stahl_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stahl-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Types">Types</span></h2>
<p>The most prominent conspiracy theories can be broadly divided into three main forms:
</p>
<ul><li>LIHOP ("Let it happen on purpose") \xe2\x80\x93 suggests that key individuals within the government had at least some foreknowledge of the attacks and deliberately ignored it or actively weakened United States\' defenses to ensure the hijacked flights were not intercepted.<sup id="cite_ref-VF_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VF-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Eleventh_Day_pp92_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Eleventh_Day_pp92-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCevolution_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCevolution-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Harbor_advance-knowledge_conspiracy_theory" title="Pearl Harbor advance-knowledge conspiracy theory">Similar allegations</a> were made about <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">Pearl Harbor</a>.</li>
<li>MIHOP ("Make/Made it happen on purpose") \xe2\x80\x93 that key individuals within the government planned the attacks and collaborated with, or framed, al-Qaeda in carrying them out. There is a range of opinions about how this might have been achieved.<sup id="cite_ref-VF_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VF-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Eleventh_Day_pp92_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Eleventh_Day_pp92-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBCevolution_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCevolution-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Others \xe2\x80\x93 who reject the accepted account of the September 11 attacks but are not proposing specific theories, but try to demonstrate that the U.S. government\'s account of the events is wrong. This, according to them, would lead to a general call for a new official investigation into the events of September 11, 2001. According to Jonathan Kay, managing editor for comment at the Canadian newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/National_Post" title="National Post">National Post</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Kay_Nashville_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kay_Nashville-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and author of <i><a href="/wiki/Among_the_Truthers" title="Among the Truthers">Among the Truthers: A Journey Through America\'s Growing Conspiracist Underground</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> "They feel their job is to show everybody that the official theory of 9/11 is wrong. And then, when everybody is convinced, then the population will rise up and demand a new investigation with government resources, and that investigation will tell us what actually happened."<sup id="cite_ref-Unofficial_Theory_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Unofficial_Theory-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Theories">Theories</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreknowledge">Foreknowledge</span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks_advance-knowledge_conspiracy_theories" title="September 11 attacks advance-knowledge conspiracy theories">September 11 attacks advance-knowledge conspiracy theories</a>; <a href="/wiki/U.S._military_response_during_the_September_11_attacks" title="U.S. military response during the September 11 attacks">U.S. military response during the September 11 attacks</a>; and <a href="/wiki/United_States_government_operations_and_exercises_on_September_11,_2001" title="United States government operations and exercises on September 11, 2001">United States government operations and exercises on September 11, 2001</a></div>
<p>Conspiracy theorists claim that action or inaction by U.S. officials with foreknowledge was intended to ensure that the attacks took place successfully. For example, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Meacher" title="Michael Meacher">Michael Meacher</a>, former British environment minister and member of <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">Tony Blair</a>\'s government, said that the United States knowingly failed to prevent the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Suspected_insider_trading">Suspected insider trading</span></h4>
<p>Some conspiracy theorists maintain that just before 9/11, an "extraordinary" amount of <a href="/wiki/Put_option" title="Put option">put options</a> were placed on <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> stocks and speculate that insiders may have known in advance of the coming events of 9/11 and placed their bets accordingly. An analysis into the possibility of <a href="/wiki/Insider_trading" title="Insider trading">insider trading</a> on 9/11 concludes that:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>A measure of abnormal long put volume was also examined and seen to be at abnormally high levels in the days leading up to the attacks. Consequently, the paper concludes that there is evidence of unusual option market activity in the days leading up to September 11 that is consistent with investors trading on advance knowledge of the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
\xe2\x80\x94Allen M. Poteshman, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Journal_of_Business" title="The Journal of Business">The Journal of Business</a></i></p></blockquote>
<p>This study was intended to address the "great deal of speculation about whether option market activity indicated that the terrorists or their associates had traded in the days leading up to September 11 on advance knowledge of the impending attacks."<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the days leading up to 9/11, analysis shows a rise in the put to call ratio for United Airlines and American Airlines, the two airlines from which planes were hijacked on 9/11. Between September 6 and 7, the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Board_Options_Exchange" title="Chicago Board Options Exchange">Chicago Board Options Exchange</a> recorded purchases of 4,744 "put" option contracts in UAL and 396 call options. On September 10, more trading in Chicago saw the purchase of 4,516 put options in American Airlines, the other airline involved in the hijackings, with a mere 748 call options in American purchased that day. No other airline companies had an unusual put to call ratio in the days leading up to the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The 9/11 Commission concluded that all these abnormal patterns in trading were coincidental.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Insurance companies saw anomalous trading activities as well. <a href="/wiki/Citigroup_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Citigroup Inc.">Citigroup Inc.</a>, which estimated that its <a href="/wiki/Travelers_Insurance" class="mw-redirect" title="Travelers Insurance">Travelers Insurance</a> unit could pay $500 million in claims from the World Trade Center attack, had about 45 times the normal volume during three trading days before the attack for options that profit, if the stock falls below $40. Citigroup shares fell $1.25 in late trading to $38.09. <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a>, which occupied 22 floors at the World Trade Center, experienced bigger-than-normal pre-attack trading of options that profited when stock prices fell. Other companies directly affected by the tragedy had similar jumps.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Raytheon" title="Raytheon">Raytheon</a>, a defense contractor, had an anomalously high number of call options trading on September 10. A Raytheon option that makes money, if shares are more than $25 each had 232 options contracts traded on the day before the attacks, almost six times the total number of trades that had occurred before that day.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The initial options were bought through at least two <a href="/wiki/Brokerage_firm" class="mw-redirect" title="Brokerage firm">brokerage firms</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Fidelity_Investments#Mutual_funds_and_stock_brokerage" title="Fidelity Investments">NFS</a>, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/Fidelity_Investments" title="Fidelity Investments">Fidelity Investments</a>, and <a href="/wiki/TD_Waterhouse" title="TD Waterhouse">TD Waterhouse</a>. It was estimated that the trader or traders would have realized a five million dollar profit. The <a href="/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Securities and Exchange Commission">Securities and Exchange Commission</a> launched an <a href="/wiki/Insider_trading" title="Insider trading">insider trading</a> investigation in which <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a> was a suspect after receiving information from at least one Wall Street Firm.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/9/11_Commission_Report" title="9/11 Commission Report">9/11 Commission Report</a> concluded that "Exhaustive investigations by the Securities and Exchange Commission, FBI, and other agencies have uncovered no evidence that anyone with advance knowledge of the attacks profited through securities transactions."<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The report further stated:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Highly publicized allegations of insider trading in advance of 9/11 generally rest on reports of unusual pre-9/11 trading activity in companies whose stock plummeted after the attacks. Some unusual trading did in fact occur, but each such trade proved to have an innocuous explanation. For example, the volume of put options \xe2\x80\x94 investments that pay off only when a stock drops in price \xe2\x80\x94 surged in the parent companies of United Airlines on September 6 and American Airlines on September 10 \xe2\x80\x94 highly suspicious trading on its face. Yet, further investigation has revealed that the trading had no connection with 9/11. A single U.S.-based institutional investor with no conceivable ties to al Qaeda purchased 95 percent of the UAL puts on September 6 as part of a trading strategy that also included <i>buying</i> 115,000 shares of American on September 10. Similarly, much of the seemingly suspicious trading in American on September 10 was traced to a specific U.S.-based options trading newsletter, faxed to its subscribers on Sunday, September 9, which recommended these trades. These examples typify the evidence examined by the investigation. The SEC and the FBI, aided by other agencies and the securities industry, devoted enormous resources to investigating this issue, including securing the cooperation of many foreign governments. These investigators have found that the apparently suspicious consistently proved innocuous.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Air-defense_stand-down_theory">Air-defense stand-down theory</span></h4>
<p>A common claim among conspiracy theorists is that the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Aerospace_Defense_Command" class="mw-redirect" title="North American Aerospace Defense Command">North American Aerospace Defense Command</a> (NORAD) issued a stand down order or deliberately scrambled fighters late to allow the hijacked airplanes to reach their targets without interference. According to this theory, NORAD had the capability of locating and intercepting planes on 9/11, and its failure to do so indicates a government conspiracy to allow the attacks to occur.<sup id="cite_ref-Mol\xc3\xa9&#124;2006_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mol\xc3\xa9|2006-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Conspiracy theorist Mark R. Elsis says: "There is only one explanation for this&#160;... Our Air Force was ordered to Stand Down on 9/11."<sup id="cite_ref-popularmechanics.com_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popularmechanics.com-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-women.timesonline.co.uk_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-women.timesonline.co.uk-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>One of the first actions taken by the hijackers on 9/11 was to turn off or disable each of the four aircraft\'s on board transponders. Without these transponder signals to identify the airplane\'s tail number, altitude, and speed, the hijacked airplanes would have been only blips among 4,500 other blips on NORAD\'s radar screens, making them very difficult to track.<sup id="cite_ref-Mol\xc3\xa9&#124;2006_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mol\xc3\xa9|2006-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDunbarReagan201133_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDunbarReagan201133-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 9/11, only 14 fighter jets were on alert in the contiguous 48 states. There was no automated method for the civilian air traffic controllers to alert NORAD.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDunbarReagan201132_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDunbarReagan201132-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> A passenger aircraft had not been hijacked in the U.S. since 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> "They had to pick up the phone and literally dial us," says Maj. Douglas Martin, public affairs officer for NORAD. Only one civilian plane\xe2\x80\x94a <a href="/wiki/1999_South_Dakota_Learjet_crash" title="1999 South Dakota Learjet crash">chartered Learjet 35</a> with golfer Payne Stewart and five others on board\xe2\x80\x94was intercepted by NORAD over North America in the decade prior to 9/11, which took one hour and 19&#160;minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDunbarReagan201138_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDunbarReagan201138-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rules in effect at that time, and on 9/11, barred supersonic flight on intercepts. Before 9/11, all other NORAD interceptions were limited to offshore <a href="/wiki/Air_Defense_Identification_Zone_(North_America)" title="Air Defense Identification Zone (North America)">Air Defense Identification Zones</a> (ADIZ). "Until 9/11 there was no domestic ADIZ," says FAA spokesman Bill Schumann. After 9/11, the FAA and NORAD increased cooperation. They set up hotlines between command centers while NORAD increased its fighter coverage and installed radar to watch airspace over the continent.<sup id="cite_ref-popularmechanics.com_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-popularmechanics.com-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The longest warning NORAD received of the hijackings was some eight minutes for American Airlines Flight 11, the first flight hijacked. The FAA alerted NORAD to the hijacked Flight 175 at just about the same time it was crashing into the World Trade Center\'s South Tower. The FAA notified NORAD of the missing \xe2\x80\x93 not hijacked \xe2\x80\x93 Flight 77 three minutes before it struck the Pentagon. NORAD received no warning of the hijack of United Flight 93 until three minutes after it had crashed in Pennsylvania.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Alleged_Communications_Leak">Alleged Communications Leak</span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Committee_for_Accuracy_in_Middle_East_Reporting_in_America" title="Committee for Accuracy in Middle East Reporting in America">CAMERA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Telegraphic_Agency" title="Jewish Telegraphic Agency">JTA (Jewish Telegraphic Agency)</a> criticized claims by <a href="/wiki/Carl_Cameron" title="Carl Cameron">Carl Cameron</a> who stated, "certain suspects in the September 11th attacks may have managed to stay ahead of them by knowing who and when investigators are calling on the telephone," by using information from <a href="/wiki/Amdocs" title="Amdocs">Amdocs Limited</a>, an Israeli-based private communications company, and <a href="/wiki/Comverse_Technology" title="Comverse Technology">Comverse Infosys</a>, another Israeli-run company that provides electronic eavesdropping technology for the U.S. government.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Israeli_agents">Israeli agents</span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks_advance-knowledge_conspiracy_theories#Israel" title="September 11 attacks advance-knowledge conspiracy theories">September 11 attacks advance-knowledge conspiracy theories \xc2\xa7&#160;Israel</a></div>
<p>It has been claimed that <a href="/wiki/Mossad" title="Mossad">Israeli agents</a> may have had foreknowledge of the attacks, and a persistent theory claimed Israeli and/or Jewish involvement.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Four hours after the attack, the FBI arrested five Israelis who had been filming the smoking skyline from the roof of a white van in the parking lot of an apartment building, for "puzzling behavior." The Israelis were videotaping the events, and one bystander said they acted in a suspicious manner: "They were like happy, you know&#160;... They didn\'t look shocked to me. I thought it was very strange." The van was found to be owned by an Israeli-owned company called Urban Moving, which the FBI believed was providing cover for an Israeli intelligence operation. The case was then moved to the FBI\'s Foreign Counterintelligence Section. According to a former CIA operations chief, "many people in the U.S. intelligence community believed that some of the men arrested were working for Israeli intelligence." A spokesperson for the Israeli Embassy in the United States said the men had not been involved in any intelligence operation in the United States. The FBI eventually concluded that the five Israelis probably had no foreknowledge of the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-White_Van_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-White_Van-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Trade_Center">World Trade Center</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_controlled_demolition_conspiracy_theories" title="World Trade Center controlled demolition conspiracy theories">World Trade Center controlled demolition conspiracy theories</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:NIST_7_WTC_Exterior_buckling.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/NIST_7_WTC_Exterior_buckling.jpg/300px-NIST_7_WTC_Exterior_buckling.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="196" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/NIST_7_WTC_Exterior_buckling.jpg/450px-NIST_7_WTC_Exterior_buckling.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/NIST_7_WTC_Exterior_buckling.jpg/600px-NIST_7_WTC_Exterior_buckling.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1498" data-file-height="978" /></a><figcaption>Criticism of the reports published by <a href="/wiki/NIST" class="mw-redirect" title="NIST">NIST</a> on the destruction of the World Trade Center buildings plays a central role in theories about an alleged controlled demolition. The picture shows the simulated exterior buckling of <a href="/wiki/7_World_Trade_Center" title="7 World Trade Center">7 WTC</a> during the collapse.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The plane crashes and resulting fires caused the <a href="/wiki/Collapse_of_the_World_Trade_Center" title="Collapse of the World Trade Center">collapse of the World Trade Center</a>. <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_controlled_demolition_conspiracy_theories" title="World Trade Center controlled demolition conspiracy theories">Controlled demolition conspiracy theories</a> say the collapse of the North Tower, South Tower, or of <a href="/wiki/7_World_Trade_Center" title="7 World Trade Center">7 World Trade Center</a> was caused by explosives installed in the buildings in advance.
</p><p>Demolition theory proponents, such as <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young_University" title="Brigham Young University">Brigham Young University</a> physicist <a href="/wiki/Steven_E._Jones" title="Steven E. Jones">Steven E. Jones</a>, architect <a href="/wiki/Richard_Gage_(architect)" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Gage (architect)">Richard Gage</a>, software engineer <a href="/wiki/Jim_Hoffman" title="Jim Hoffman">Jim Hoffman</a>, and theologian <a href="/wiki/David_Ray_Griffin" title="David Ray Griffin">David Ray Griffin</a>, argue that the aircraft impacts and resulting fires could not have weakened the buildings sufficiently to initiate a catastrophic collapse, and that the buildings would not have collapsed completely, nor at the speeds that they did, without additional factors weakening the structures.
</p><p>In the article "Active Thermotic Material Discovered in Dust from the 9/11 World Trade Center Catastrophe", which appeared in the <i>Open Chemical Physics Journal</i>, authors Niels Harrit of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Copenhagen" title="University of Copenhagen">University of Copenhagen</a>\'s Department of Chemistry, Jeffrey Farrer of <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young_University" title="Brigham Young University">Brigham Young University</a>\'s Department of Physics and Astronomy, Steven E. Jones, and others state that <a href="/wiki/Thermite" title="Thermite">thermite</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nano-thermite" title="Nano-thermite">nano-thermite</a> composites in the dust and debris were found following the collapse of the three buildings. The article contained no scientific rebuttal and the editor in chief of the publication subsequently resigned.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTCountersTheories_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTCountersTheories-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Deseret-Dean-2006_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deseret-Dean-2006-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jones has not explained how the amount of explosive needed to bring down the buildings could have been positioned in the two buildings without drawing attention, but mentioned efforts to research the buildings\' maintenance activity in the weeks prior to the event. Federal investigators at the National Institute of Standards and Technology state that enormous quantities of thermite would have to be applied to the structural columns to damage them, but Jones disputed this, saying that he and others were investigating "superthermite".<sup id="cite_ref-NYTCountersTheories_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTCountersTheories-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Brent Blanchard, author of "A History of Explosive Demolition in America",<sup id="cite_ref-HEDA_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HEDA-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> who corresponded with Jones, states that questions about the viability of Jones\' theories remain unanswered, such as the fact that no demolition personnel noticed any telltale signs of thermite during the eight months of debris removal following the towers\' collapse. Blanchard also said that a verifiable chain of possession needs to be established for the tested beams, which did not occur with the beams Jones tested, raising questions of whether the metal pieces tested could have been cut away from the debris pile with acetylene torches, shears, or other potentially contaminated equipment while on site, or exposed to trace amounts of thermite or other compounds while being handled, while in storage, or while being transferred from Ground Zero to memorial sites.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:9_11_underground_fires_Hotslag-300x215.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ea/9_11_underground_fires_Hotslag-300x215.jpg/220px-9_11_underground_fires_Hotslag-300x215.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/ea/9_11_underground_fires_Hotslag-300x215.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="215" /></a><figcaption>Excavating equipment was cooled by water spray due to concerns about melting from underground fires.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Jones also said that molten steel found in the rubble was evidence of explosives, as an ordinary airplane fire would not generate enough heat to produce this, citing photographs of red debris being removed by construction equipment, but Blanchard said that if there had been any molten steel in the rubble any excavation equipment encountering it would have been immediately damaged.<sup id="cite_ref-NYTCountersTheories_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTCountersTheories-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Other sampling of the pulverized dust by <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">United States Geological Survey</a> and RJ Lee did not report any evidence of thermite or explosives. It has been theorized the "thermite material" found was primer paint.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCMag_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCMag-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Dave Thomas of <i><a href="/wiki/Skeptical_Inquirer" title="Skeptical Inquirer">Skeptical Inquirer</a></i> magazine, noting that the residue in question was claimed to be thermotic because of its iron oxide and aluminum composition, pointed out that these substances are found in many items common to the towers. Thomas said that in order to cut through a vertical steel beam, special high-temperature containment must be added to prevent the molten iron from dropping down, and that the thermite reaction is too slow for it to be practically used in building demolition. Thomas pointed out that when <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Ventura" title="Jesse Ventura">Jesse Ventura</a> hired <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_Institute_of_Mining_and_Technology" title="New Mexico Institute of Mining and Technology">New Mexico Tech</a> to conduct a demonstration showing nanothermite slicing through a large steel beam, the nanothermite produced copious flame and smoke but no damage to the beam, even though it was in a horizontal, and therefore optimal, position.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Standards_and_Technology" title="National Institute of Standards and Technology">National Institute of Standards and Technology</a> (NIST) concluded the accepted version was more than sufficient to explain the collapse of the buildings. NIST and many scientists have refused to debate conspiracy theorists because they feel it would give those theories unwarranted credibility.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Specialists in structural mechanics and structural engineering accept the model of a fire-induced, gravity-driven collapse of the World Trade Center buildings without the use of explosives.<sup id="cite_ref-bazant07_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bazant07-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ProfessorsOfParanoia_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProfessorsOfParanoia-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-conspiraciesContinueToAbound_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-conspiraciesContinueToAbound-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> As a result, NIST said that it did not perform any test for the residue of explosive compounds of any kind in the debris.<sup id="cite_ref-nistfaq_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nistfaq-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Soon after the day of the attacks, major media sources published that the towers had collapsed due to heat melting the steel.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Melt_Steel_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Melt_Steel-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NewScientist_Melt_Steel_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewScientist_Melt_Steel-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
The erroneous claim that the combustion temperature of jet fuel could not melt steel contributed to the belief among skeptics that the towers would not have collapsed without external interference. The basic claim is false, because the <a href="/wiki/Adiabatic_flame_temperature" title="Adiabatic flame temperature">combustion temperature of kerosene</a> (jet fuel) is, in fact, more than 500&#160;\xc2\xb0C higher than the <a href="/wiki/Structural_steel#Thermal_properties" title="Structural steel">melting point of structural steel</a> (2093&#160;\xc2\xb0C <i>vs.</i> less than 1539&#160;\xc2\xb0C).
</p><p>Further, NIST did not claim that the steel melted, but rather that heat softened and weakened the steel, and that weakening, together with the damage caused by the planes\' impacts, caused structural collapse.<sup id="cite_ref-nistfaq_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nistfaq-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> NIST reported that a simulation model based on the simple assumption that combustible vapors burned immediately upon mixing with the incoming air showed that "at any given location, the duration of gas temperatures near 1,000&#160;\xc2\xb0C was about 15 to 20 minutes. The rest of the time, the calculated temperatures were 500&#160;\xc2\xb0C or below."<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pentagon">Pentagon</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><span><video id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Pentagon_Security_Camera_1.ogv/220px-seek%3D91-Pentagon_Security_Camera_1.ogv.jpg" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="220" height="149" data-durationhint="192" data-mwtitle="Pentagon_Security_Camera_1.ogv" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" resource="/wiki/File:Pentagon_Security_Camera_1.ogv"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/67/Pentagon_Security_Camera_1.ogv" type="video/ogg; codecs=&quot;theora&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file, 312 \xc3\x97 212 (258 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="312" data-height="212" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/6/67/Pentagon_Security_Camera_1.ogv/Pentagon_Security_Camera_1.ogv.120p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-title="Lowest bandwidth VP9 (120P)" data-shorttitle="VP9 120P" data-transcodekey="120p.vp9.webm" data-width="176" data-height="120" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/6/67/Pentagon_Security_Camera_1.ogv/Pentagon_Security_Camera_1.ogv.160p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;" data-title="Low bandwidth WebM (160P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 160P" data-transcodekey="160p.webm" data-width="236" data-height="160" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/6/67/Pentagon_Security_Camera_1.ogv/Pentagon_Security_Camera_1.ogv.180p.vp9.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp9, opus&quot;" data-title="Low bandwidth VP9 (180P)" data-shorttitle="VP9 180P" data-transcodekey="180p.vp9.webm" data-width="264" data-height="180" /></video></span><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Security_camera" class="mw-redirect" title="Security camera">Security camera</a> footage of Flight 77 hitting the Pentagon (at 1:26 in the video)</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pentagon.Nach_Einsturz.Rasen.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Pentagon.Nach_Einsturz.Rasen.jpg/220px-Pentagon.Nach_Einsturz.Rasen.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="117" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Pentagon.Nach_Einsturz.Rasen.jpg/330px-Pentagon.Nach_Einsturz.Rasen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Pentagon.Nach_Einsturz.Rasen.jpg/440px-Pentagon.Nach_Einsturz.Rasen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2813" data-file-height="1500" /></a><figcaption>The Pentagon, after collapse of the damaged section</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Flight_77_wreckage_at_Pentagon.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Flight_77_wreckage_at_Pentagon.jpg/220px-Flight_77_wreckage_at_Pentagon.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Flight_77_wreckage_at_Pentagon.jpg/330px-Flight_77_wreckage_at_Pentagon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Flight_77_wreckage_at_Pentagon.jpg/440px-Flight_77_wreckage_at_Pentagon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>Airplane <a href="/wiki/Debris" title="Debris">debris</a> scattered near the Pentagon on the day of the attack</figcaption></figure>
<p>Political activist <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Meyssan" title="Thierry Meyssan">Thierry Meyssan</a> and filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Dylan_Avery" class="mw-redirect" title="Dylan Avery">Dylan Avery</a> claim that <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines_Flight_77" title="American Airlines Flight 77">American Airlines Flight 77</a> did not crash into <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">the Pentagon</a>. Instead, they argue that the Pentagon was hit by a missile launched by elements from inside the U.S. government. Some claim that the holes in the Pentagon walls were far too small to have been made by a Boeing 757: "How does a plane 125&#160;ft. wide and 155&#160;ft. long fit into a hole which is only 60&#160;ft. across?" Meyssan\'s book, <i>L\'Effroyable Imposture</i> (published in English as <i>9/11: The Big Lie</i>) became available in more than a dozen languages. When released, the book was heavily criticized by both the mainstream French and American press, and later, from within the <a href="/wiki/9/11_Truth_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11 Truth movement">9/11 Truth movement</a>. The French newspaper <i>Liberation</i> called the book "a tissue of wild and irresponsible allegations, entirely without foundation."<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ConspiracyTheoristsDownButNotOut_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ConspiracyTheoristsDownButNotOut-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In response to the conspiracy theorists\' claim of a missile hitting the Pentagon, Mete Sozen, a professor of civil engineering at <a href="/wiki/Purdue_University" title="Purdue University">Purdue University</a> argues that: "A crashing jet doesn\'t punch a cartoon-like outline of itself into a reinforced concrete building. When Flight 77 hit the Pentagon, one wing hit the ground and the other was sheared off by the Pentagon\'s load-bearing columns."<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/ArchitectureWeek" title="ArchitectureWeek">ArchitectureWeek</a></i>, the reason the Pentagon took relatively little damage from the impact was because Wedge One had recently been renovated.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> (This was part of a renovation program which had been begun in the 1980s, and Wedge One was the first of five to be renovated.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>)
</p><p>Evidence contradicting some conspiracy theorists\' claim of a missile hitting the Pentagon have been described by researchers within the 9/11 Truth Movement, such as Jim Hoffman, in his essay "The Pentagon Attack: What the Physical Evidence Shows", and by others broadly refuting the role of other conspiracies in the attacks. The evidence refuting missile claims includes airplane debris including Flight 77\'s <a href="/wiki/Flight_recorder" title="Flight recorder">black boxes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> the nose cone, landing gear,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> an airplane tire,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> and an intact cockpit seat<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> were observed at the crash site. The remains of passengers from Flight 77 were indeed found at the Pentagon crash site and their identities confirmed by <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> analysis.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Foreign governments, such as the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the People&#39;s Republic of China">Chinese Foreign Ministry</a> (FMPRC), also confirms the death of their citizens onboard Flight 77.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Many eyewitnesses saw the plane strike the Pentagon. Further, Flight 77 passengers made phone calls reporting that their airplane had been hijacked. For example, passenger Renee May called her mother to tell her that the plane had been hijacked and that the passengers had been herded to the back of the plane. Another passenger named <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Olson" title="Barbara Olson">Barbara Olson</a> called her husband (U.S. Solicitor General <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Olson" title="Theodore Olson">Theodore Olson</a>) and said that the flight had been hijacked, and that the hijackers had <a href="/wiki/Knives" class="mw-redirect" title="Knives">knives</a> and <a href="/wiki/Box_cutters" class="mw-redirect" title="Box cutters">box cutters</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-usgovDidPlaneHitPentagon_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usgovDidPlaneHitPentagon-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Some conspiracy theories say the phone calls the passengers made were fabricated by voice morphing, the passengers\' bodies disposed of, and a missile fired at the Pentagon.<sup id="cite_ref-Dunbar&#124;Reagan&#124;2011_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dunbar|Reagan|2011-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The pressure group <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Watch" title="Judicial Watch">Judicial Watch</a> filed a <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_Information_Act_(United_States)" title="Freedom of Information Act (United States)">Freedom of Information Act</a> request on December 15, 2004, to force the government to release video recordings from the Sheraton National Hotel, the Nexcomm/Citgo gas station, Pentagon security cameras and the Virginia Department of Transportation. On May 16, 2006, the government released the Pentagon security camera videos to Judicial Watch.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The image of American Airlines Flight 77 which appears in the videos has been described as "[a] white blob" and "a white streak" (by the BBC),<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> "a thin white blur" (by The <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> and "a silver speck low to the ground" (in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> A sequence of five frames from one of the videos already appeared in the media in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Some conspiracy theorists believe the new video does not answer their questions.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flight_93">Flight 93</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:UA93_crash_site.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/UA93_crash_site.jpg/220px-UA93_crash_site.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/UA93_crash_site.jpg/330px-UA93_crash_site.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/UA93_crash_site.jpg/440px-UA93_crash_site.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1487" data-file-height="1001" /></a><figcaption>Flight 93 crash site</figcaption></figure>
<p>The fourth plane hijacked on 9/11, <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines_Flight_93" title="United Airlines Flight 93">United Airlines Flight 93</a>, crashed in an open field near <a href="/wiki/Shanksville" class="mw-redirect" title="Shanksville">Shanksville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, after the passengers revolted. Out of the four planes hijacked on that day, Flight 93 was the only one not to reach its target.<sup id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>One conspiracy theory surrounding this event is the claim that Flight 93 was shot down by a U.S. fighter jet. <a href="/wiki/David_Ray_Griffin" title="David Ray Griffin">David Ray Griffin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alex_Jones" title="Alex Jones">Alex Jones</a> have asserted that large parts of the plane, including the main body of the engine, landed miles away from the main wreckage site, too far away for an ordinary plane crash. Jones says that planes usually leave a small debris field when they crash, and that this is not compatible with reports of wreckage found farther away from the main crash site. One person claimed that the main body of the engine was found miles away from the main wreckage site with damage comparable to that which a heat-seeking missile would do to an airliner.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_100-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to some theories, the plane had to be shot down by the government because passengers had found out about the alleged plot.<sup id="cite_ref-women.timesonline.co.uk_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-women.timesonline.co.uk-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Phil Mol\xc3\xa9 of <i><a href="/wiki/Skeptic_(U.S._magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Skeptic (U.S. magazine)">Skeptic</a></i> magazine, "[this] claim rests largely on unsupported assertions that the main body of the engine and other large parts of the plane turned up miles from the main wreckage site, too far away to have resulted from an ordinary crash. This claim is incorrect, because the engine was found only 300&#160;yards from the main crash site, and its location was consistent with the direction in which the plane had been traveling."<sup id="cite_ref-Mol\xc3\xa9&#124;2006_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mol\xc3\xa9|2006-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Michael K. Hynes, an airline accident expert who investigated the crash of <a href="/wiki/TWA_Flight_800" title="TWA Flight 800">TWA Flight 800</a> in 1996, says that, at very high velocities of 500&#160;mph or more, it would only take a few seconds to move or tumble across the ground for 300&#160;yards.<sup id="cite_ref-Mol\xc3\xa9&#124;2006_76-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mol\xc3\xa9|2006-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_100-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Reports of wreckage discovered at Indian Lake by local residents are accurate. CNN reported that investigators found debris from the crash at least eight miles away from the crash site, including in <a href="/wiki/New_Baltimore,_Pennsylvania" title="New Baltimore, Pennsylvania">New Baltimore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> According to CNN, this debris was all very light material that the wind would have easily blown away, and a <i>Pittsburgh Post-Gazette</i> article from September 14, 2001, describes the material as "mostly papers", "strands of charred insulation", and an "endorsed paycheck". The same article quotes FBI agent Bill Crowley that, "Lighter, smaller debris probably shot into the air on the heat of a fireball that witnesses said shot several hundred feet into the air after the jetliner crashed. Then, it probably rode a wind that was blowing southeast at about 9&#160;m.p.h."<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Also, the distance between the crash site and Indian Lake was misreported in some accounts. According to the BBC, "In a straight line, Indian Lake is just over a mile from the crash site. The road between the two locations takes a roundabout route of 6.9&#160;miles\xe2\x80\x94accounting for the erroneous reports."<sup id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some conspiracy theorists believe a small white jet seen flying over the crash area may have fired a missile to shoot down Flight 93.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="In the reference, no one specifically theorizes that the &quot;small white jet&quot; observed by witnesses committed a shootdown. An Air Force jet or a U.S. Customs airplane are conjectured. http&#58;//www.popularmechanics.com/science/defense/1227842.html?page=7 (December 2009)">dubious</span></a>&#32;<span class="metadata"> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Talk:9/11_conspiracy_theories#Dubious" title="Talk:9/11 conspiracy theories">discuss</a></span></i>&#93;</sup> Government agencies such as the FBI assert this small plane was a <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Falcon" title="Dassault Falcon">Dassault Falcon</a> business jet asked to descend to an altitude of around 1,500&#160;ft to survey the impact.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Ben Sliney, who was the FAA operation manager on September 11, 2001, says no military aircraft were near Flight 93.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some internet videos, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Loose_Change_(film_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Loose Change (film series)">Loose Change</a></i>, speculate that Flight 93 safely landed in <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">Ohio</a>, and a substituted plane was involved in the crash in Pennsylvania. Often cited is a preliminary news report that Flight 93 landed at a <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">Cleveland</a> airport;<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> it was later learned that Delta Flight 1989 was the plane confused with Flight 93, and the report was retracted as inaccurate. Several websites within the 9/11 Truth Movement dispute this claim, citing the wreckage at the scene, eyewitness testimony, and the difficulty of secretly substituting one plane for another, and claim that such "hoax theories&#160;... appear calculated to alienate victims\' survivors and the larger public from the 9/11 truth movement". The editor of the article has since written a <a href="/wiki/Rebuttal" title="Rebuttal">rebuttal</a> to the claims.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Valencia McClatchey, a local woman who took the only photograph of the mushroom cloud from the impact of Flight 93 seconds after it hit the ground, says she has been harassed over the telephone and in person by conspiracy theorists, who claim she faked the photo. The FBI, the Somerset County authorities, the Smithsonian, and the National Park Service\'s Flight 93 National Memorial staff have all individually examined the photograph as well as the film negatives and all four agencies consider the photo to be authentic.<sup id="cite_ref-Flight93Photo_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flight93Photo-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While some conspiracy theorists have claimed that passengers of Flight 93 and/or <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines_Flight_77" title="American Airlines Flight 77">Flight 77</a> were murdered or that they were relocated, with the intent that they never be found,<sup id="cite_ref-women.timesonline.co.uk_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-women.timesonline.co.uk-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> others within the 9/11 Truth Movement, such as <a href="/wiki/Jim_Hoffman" title="Jim Hoffman">Jim Hoffman</a> and <a href="/wiki/9/11_Truth_Movement#Scholars_for_9/11_Truth_&amp;_Justice" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11 Truth Movement">Scholars for 9/11 Truth &amp; Justice</a>, repudiate such claims.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hijackers">Hijackers</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hijackers_in_the_September_11_attacks" title="Hijackers in the September 11 attacks">Hijackers in the September 11 attacks</a> and <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks_advance-knowledge_conspiracy_theories" title="September 11 attacks advance-knowledge conspiracy theories">September 11 attacks advance-knowledge conspiracy theories</a></div>
