<p>During the initial confusion surrounding the immediate aftermath of the September 11 attacks, the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> published the names and identities of what they believed to be some of the hijackers.<sup id="cite_ref-911Ct_SteveHerrmann_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-911Ct_SteveHerrmann-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Some of the people named were later discovered to be alive, a fact that was seized upon by 9/11 conspiracy theorists as proof that the hijackings were faked.<sup id="cite_ref-911Ct_SteveHerrmann_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-911Ct_SteveHerrmann-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Panoply_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Panoply-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The BBC explained that the initial confusion may have arisen because the names they reported back in 2001 were common Arabic and Islamic names.<sup id="cite_ref-911Ct_SteveHerrmann_132-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-911Ct_SteveHerrmann-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In response to a request from the BBC, the FBI said that it was confident to have identified all nineteen hijackers, and that none of the other inquiries had raised the issue of doubt about their identities.<sup id="cite_ref-911Ct_SteveHerrmann_132-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-911Ct_SteveHerrmann-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> also acknowledged these as cases of mistaken identity.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to John Bradley, the former managing editor of <i>Arab News</i> in Jeddah, Saudi Arabia, the only public information about the hijackers was a list of names issued by the FBI on September 14, 2001. When the FBI released photographs four days after the cited reports on September 27, the mistaken identities were quickly resolved. According to Bradley, "all of this is attributable to the chaos that prevailed during the first few days following the attack. What we\'re dealing with are coincidentally identical names." In Saudi Arabia, says Bradley, the names of two of the allegedly surviving attackers, <a href="/wiki/Said_al-Ghamdi" class="mw-redirect" title="Said al-Ghamdi">Said al-Ghamdi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Walid_al-Shari" class="mw-redirect" title="Walid al-Shari">Walid al-Shari</a>, are "as common as John Smith in the United States or Great Britain."<sup id="cite_ref-Panoply_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Panoply-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Thomas Kean, chair of the 9/11 Commission, "Sixteen of the nineteen shouldn\'t have gotten into the United States in any way at all because there was something wrong with their visas, something wrong with their passports. They should simply have been stopped at the border. That was sixteen of the nineteen. Obviously, if even half of those people had been stopped, there never would have been a plot."<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Khalid al Mihdhar and Nawaf al Hazmi had both been identified as al-Qaeda agents by the CIA, but that information was not shared with the FBI or U.S. Immigration, so both men were able to legally enter the U.S. to prepare for the 9/11 attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_governments">Foreign governments</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Saddam_Hussein_and_al-Qaeda_link_allegations" class="mw-redirect" title="Saddam Hussein and al-Qaeda link allegations">Saddam Hussein and al-Qaeda link allegations</a> and <a href="/wiki/9/11_advanced-knowledge_debate#Foreign_government_foreknowledge" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11 advanced-knowledge debate">Foreign government foreknowledge</a></div>
<p>There are allegations that individuals within the Pakistani <a href="/wiki/Inter-Services_Intelligence" title="Inter-Services Intelligence">Inter-Services Intelligence</a> (ISI) may have played an important role in <a href="/wiki/Responsibility_for_the_September_11_attacks#Financing_the_attacks" title="Responsibility for the September 11 attacks">financing the attacks</a>. There are also claims that other foreign intelligence agencies, such as the Israeli <a href="/wiki/Mossad" title="Mossad">Mossad</a>, had foreknowledge of the attacks, and that Saudi Arabia may have played a role in financing the attacks. General <a href="/wiki/Hamid_Gul" title="Hamid Gul">Hamid Gul</a>, a former head of ISI, believes the attacks were an "inside job" originating in the United States, perpetrated by Israel or <a href="/wiki/Neo-conservative" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-conservative">neo-conservatives</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Cossiga" title="Francesco Cossiga">Francesco Cossiga</a>, former President of Italy from 1985 until his 1992 resignation over <a href="/wiki/Operation_Gladio" title="Operation Gladio">Operation Gladio</a>, said that it is common knowledge among the Italian center-left that the 9/11 attacks were a joint operation of the CIA and the Mossad.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Subsequent reports indicated that he did not actually believe this.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Israel">Israel</span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks_advance-knowledge_conspiracy_theories#Israel" title="September 11 attacks advance-knowledge conspiracy theories">September 11 attacks advance-knowledge conspiracy theories: Israel</a></div>
<p>A conspiracy theory documented by the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">Anti-Defamation League</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_Encyclopedia" title="Conspiracy Encyclopedia">Thom Burnett</a> and others is that the state of Israel was involved in the attacks, and may have planned them. A variety of motives are suggested, including: to cause the United States to attack enemies of Israel; to divert public attention away from Israel\'s treatment of <a href="/wiki/Palestinians" title="Palestinians">Palestinians</a>; to help <a href="/wiki/Zionists" class="mw-redirect" title="Zionists">Zionists</a> take control of world affairs; and to persuade Americans to support Israel. Variants of the theory contend that the attack was organized by <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Sharon" title="Ariel Sharon">Ariel Sharon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mossad" title="Mossad">Mossad</a>, or the government of Israel.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mutations_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mutations-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Kevin Barrett, a former lecturer at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Wisconsin">University of Wisconsin</a> is, according to <i><a href="/wiki/Slate_(magazine)" title="Slate (magazine)">Slate</a></i> website, a "leading advocate of theories that Israel\'s Mossad orchestrated the 9/11 attacks."<sup id="cite_ref-SlateMainstream_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SlateMainstream-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some proponents of this believe that Jewish employees were forewarned by Israeli intelligence to skip work on September 11, resulting in no Jewish deaths at the World Trade Center. According to Cinnamon Stillwell, some 9/11 conspiracy theorists put this number as high as 4,000 Jewish people skipping work.<sup id="cite_ref-sfgateTruthAbout911ConspiracyTheories_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sfgateTruthAbout911ConspiracyTheories-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> This was first reported on September 17 by the Lebanese <a href="/wiki/Hezbollah" title="Hezbollah">Hezbollah</a>-owned satellite television channel <a href="/wiki/Al-Manar" title="Al-Manar">Al-Manar</a> and is believed to be based on the September 12 edition of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jerusalem_Post" title="The Jerusalem Post">The Jerusalem Post</a></i> that said "The Foreign Ministry in Jerusalem has so far received the names of 4,000 Israelis believed to have been in the areas of the World Trade Center and the Pentagon at the time of the attacks."<sup id="cite_ref-jews_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jews-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The number of Jews who died in the attacks is variously estimated at between 270 and 400.<sup id="cite_ref-jews_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jews-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-phas-13_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phas-13-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The lower figure tracks closely with the percentage of Jews living in the New York area and partial surveys of the victims\' listed religion. The U.S. State Department has published a partial list of 76 in response to claims that fewer Jews/Israelis died in the WTC attacks than should have been present at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-jews_146-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jews-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-usgov4000JewsRumor_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usgov4000JewsRumor-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Five Israeli citizens died in the attack.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Antisemitism_in_conspiracy_theories">Antisemitism in conspiracy theories</span></h4>
<p>In 2003, the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">Anti-Defamation League</a> (ADL) published a report attacking "hateful conspiracy theories" that the 9/11 attacks were carried about by Israelis and Jews, saying they had the potential to "rationalize and fuel global <a href="/wiki/Anti-Semitism" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Semitism">anti-Semitism</a>." It found that such theories were widely accepted in the <a href="/wiki/Arab_conspiracy_theories" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab conspiracy theories">Arab and Muslim world</a>, as well as in Europe and the United States.
</p><p>The ADL\'s report found that "The Big Lie has united American <a href="/wiki/Far-right_politics" title="Far-right politics">far-right</a> extremists and <a href="/wiki/White_supremacy" title="White supremacy">white supremacists</a> and elements within the Arab and Muslim world". It asserted that many of the theories were modern manifestation of the 19th-century <i><a href="/wiki/Protocols_of_the_Elders_of_Zion" class="mw-redirect" title="Protocols of the Elders of Zion">Protocols of the Elders of Zion</a></i>, which purported to map out a Jewish conspiracy for world domination.<sup id="cite_ref-mutations_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mutations-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The ADL has characterized the <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Rense" title="Jeff Rense">Jeff Rense</a> website as carrying anti-Semitic materials, such as "American Jews staged the 9/11 terrorist attacks for their own financial gain and to induce the American people to endorse wars of aggression and <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a> on the nations of the Middle East and the theft of their resources for the benefit of Israel".<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Pedro A. Sanjuan, a former <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> diplomat, alleged that antisemitic 9/11 conspiracy theories were quite common at high levels of the organization following the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Saudi_Arabia">Saudi Arabia</span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Alleged_Saudi_government_role_in_the_September_11_attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="Alleged Saudi government role in the September 11 attacks">Alleged Saudi government role in the September 11 attacks</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_28_pages" title="The 28 pages">The 28 pages</a></div>
<p>British investigative journalists <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Summers" title="Anthony Summers">Anthony Summers</a> and Robbyn Swan claimed in their 2011 book <i>The Eleventh Day</i> that the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Royal_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="Saudi Royal Family">Saudi Royal Family</a> provided material and financial support to the hijackers and that the Bush Administration covered this up as well as their own alleged incompetence. The authors claim the <a href="/wiki/9/11_Truth_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11 Truth movement">9/11 Truth movement</a> helped this coverup by deflecting attention away from these actions.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> In September 2011 a "Lloyd\'s insurance syndicate" began legal action against Saudi Arabia demanding the repayment of \xc2\xa3136m it paid out to victims of the 9/11 attacks. A number of prominent Saudi charities and banks as well as a leading member of the al-Saud royal family were accused of being "agents and alter egos" for the Saudi state that "knowingly" provided funding to al-Qaeda and encouraged anti Western sentiment.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Such theories have historically revolved around the putative content of the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Inquiry_into_Intelligence_Community_Activities_before_and_after_the_Terrorist_Attacks_of_September_11,_2001#Redacted_sections" title="Joint Inquiry into Intelligence Community Activities before and after the Terrorist Attacks of September 11, 2001">28 pages</a> of the 2002 report of the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Inquiry_into_Intelligence_Community_Activities_before_and_after_the_Terrorist_Attacks_of_September_11,_2001" title="Joint Inquiry into Intelligence Community Activities before and after the Terrorist Attacks of September 11, 2001">U.S. Congress Joint Inquiry</a><sup id="cite_ref-post2013_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post2013-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> that were withheld from publication until July 15, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-WaPoRelease_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WaPoRelease-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Former Florida Senator <a href="/wiki/Bob_Graham" title="Bob Graham">Bob Graham</a>, co-chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Inquiry_into_Intelligence_Community_Activities_before_and_after_the_Terrorist_Attacks_of_September_11,_2001" title="Joint Inquiry into Intelligence Community Activities before and after the Terrorist Attacks of September 11, 2001">Joint Inquiry</a>, as well as other former officials who did read the entire version of the Joint Inquiry\'s report, still partly classified, believe there is a U.S. government\'s coverup on the Saudi government officials\' substantial aid provided to the perpetrators of the 9/11 act,<sup id="cite_ref-post2013_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-post2013-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> notably the role of Fahad al-Thumairy, a diplomat at the Saudi consulate in Los Angeles.<sup id="cite_ref-locked_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-locked-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="No-planes_theory">No-planes theory</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Noseoutframe.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b8/Noseoutframe.jpg/220px-Noseoutframe.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b8/Noseoutframe.jpg/330px-Noseoutframe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b8/Noseoutframe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="407" data-file-height="244" /></a><figcaption>The "no-plane theory", promoted via Internet videos, claims that this shot of the second impact, taken from a news helicopter, depicts a video composite of a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767</a> accidentally appearing from behind a <a href="/wiki/Layers_(digital_image_editing)#Layer_Mask" title="Layers (digital image editing)">Layer Mask</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Former chief economist within the Labor Department under the Bush administration, <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Reynolds" title="Morgan Reynolds">Morgan Reynolds</a>, argues that no planes were used in the attacks. Reynolds claims it is physically impossible that the Boeing planes of Flights 11 and 175 could have penetrated the steel frames of the Towers, and that <a href="/wiki/Digital_compositing" title="Digital compositing">digital compositing</a> was used to depict the plane crashes in both news reports and subsequent amateur video. "There were no planes, there were no hijackers", Reynolds insists. "I know, I know, I\'m out of the mainstream, but that\'s the way it is". According to <a href="/wiki/David_Shayler" title="David Shayler">David Shayler</a>, "the only explanation is that they were missiles surrounded by holograms made to look like planes", he says, which would be well beyond the capabilities of contemporaneous <a href="/wiki/Hologram" class="mw-redirect" title="Hologram">hologram</a> technology. "Watch footage frame by frame and you will see a cigar-shaped missile hitting the World Trade Center". Most no-planes adherents, including <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Meyssan" title="Thierry Meyssan">Thierry Meyssan</a> and Reynolds, assert that either CGI of a passenger plane was overlaid onto a winged cruise missile or military aircraft, or that computer-generated images of a passenger plane were inserted into the video footage and plane-shaped explosive cut-outs were planted in the buildings in order to create the impression of plane impact.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Some truth movement veterans have repeatedly refuted the "no-plane" claims.<sup id="cite_ref-women.timesonline.co.uk_77-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-women.timesonline.co.uk-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-msnbc_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msnbc-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> In fact, discussion of no-plane theories has been banned from certain conspiracy theory websites and advocates have sometimes been threatened with violence by posters at other conspiracy theory websites.<sup id="cite_ref-Yoda_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yoda-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cover-up_allegations">Cover-up allegations</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cockpit_recorders">Cockpit recorders</span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Flight_77_CVR.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flight_77_CVR.jpg/220px-Flight_77_CVR.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="200" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flight_77_CVR.jpg/330px-Flight_77_CVR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Flight_77_CVR.jpg/440px-Flight_77_CVR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="820" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Cockpit_voice_recorder" class="mw-redirect" title="Cockpit voice recorder">cockpit voice recorder</a> from <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines_Flight_77" title="American Airlines Flight 77">Flight 77</a> was heavily damaged from the impact and resulting fire.</figcaption></figure>
<p>According to the 9/11 Commission Report, both black boxes from Flight 77 and both black boxes from Flight 93 were recovered. Flight 77\'s CVR was said to be too damaged to yield any data. On April 18, 2002, the FBI allowed the families of victims from Flight 93 to listen to the voice recordings.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> In April 2006, a transcript of the CVR was released as part of the <a href="/wiki/Zacarias_Moussaoui" title="Zacarias Moussaoui">Zacarias Moussaoui</a> trial.<sup id="cite_ref-United93FullTranscript_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United93FullTranscript-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Two men, Michael Bellone and Nicholas DeMasi, who worked extensively in the wreckage of the World Trade Center, said in the book <i>Behind-The-Scenes: Ground Zero</i> that they helped federal agents find three of the four "black boxes" from the jetliners:<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"><blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>At one point, I was assigned to take Federal Agents around the site to search for the black boxes from the planes. We were getting ready to go out. My ATV was parked at the top of the stairs at the Brooks Brothers entrance area. We loaded up about a million dollars worth of equipment and strapped it into the ATV. There were a total of four black boxes. We found three.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bin_Laden_tapes">Bin Laden tapes</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Videos_of_Osama_bin_Laden" class="mw-redirect" title="Videos of Osama bin Laden">Videos of Osama bin Laden</a></div>
<p>A series of interviews, audio and videotapes were released in the years following the 9/11 attacks that were reported to be from Osama bin Laden. In the first of these the speaker denied responsibility for the attacks. On September 17, 2001, in a statement issued to <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera" title="Al Jazeera">Al Jazeera</a>, Bin Laden is quoted as saying: "The U.S. government has consistently blamed me for being behind every occasion its enemies attack it. I would like to assure the world that I did not plan the recent attacks, which seems to have been planned by people for personal reasons."<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a tape released in December 2001 known as \'the <a href="/wiki/Jalalabad" title="Jalalabad">Jalalabad</a> tape\', the speaker is alleged to have foreknowledge of the attacks. The <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> claimed the tape was probably from <a href="/wiki/Osama_bin_Laden" title="Osama bin Laden">Osama bin Laden</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Some observers, especially people in the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_world" title="Muslim world">Muslim world</a>, doubted the authenticity of the tape.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> On December 20, 2001, German TV channel "<a href="/wiki/Das_Erste" title="Das Erste">Das Erste</a>" broadcast an analysis of the White House\'s translation of the videotape. On the program <i>Monitor</i>, two independent translators and an expert on <a href="/wiki/Oriental_Studies" class="mw-redirect" title="Oriental Studies">Oriental Studies</a> found the White House\'s translation to be both inaccurate and manipulative, stating, "At the most important places where it is held to prove the guilt of bin Laden, it is not identical with the Arabic", and that the words used that indicate foreknowledge can not be heard at all in the original. Prof. Gernot Rotter, professor of Islamic and Arabic Studies at the Asia-Africa Institute at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hamburg" title="University of Hamburg">University of Hamburg</a>, said "The American translators who listened to the tapes and transcribed them apparently wrote a lot of things in that they wanted to hear but that cannot be heard on the tape no matter how many times you listen to it."<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
Some members of <a href="/wiki/Scholars_for_9/11_Truth" class="mw-redirect" title="Scholars for 9/11 Truth">Scholars for 9/11 Truth</a> believe that the man in this videotape is not Osama bin Laden at all, citing differences in weight and facial features, along with his wearing of a gold ring, which is forbidden by Muslim law, and writing with his right hand although bin Laden was left-handed.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an audiotape released in November 2007, Bin Laden claimed responsibility for the attacks and denied the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> and the Afghan government or people had any prior knowledge of the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated5_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated5-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Reuters-Voice_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-Voice-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with al-Jazeera, <a href="/wiki/Khalid_Sheikh_Mohammed" title="Khalid Sheikh Mohammed">Khalid Sheikh Mohammed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ramzi_bin_al-Shibh" title="Ramzi bin al-Shibh">Ramzi bin al-Shibh</a>, two of al-Qaeda\'s alleged masterminds of the attacks, also confessed their involvement in the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="CIA_recruitment_efforts">CIA recruitment efforts</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Richard_A._Clarke" title="Richard A. Clarke">Richard Clarke</a>, who headed the government\'s anti-terrorism efforts in 2001, theorized CIA director <a href="/wiki/George_Tenet" title="George Tenet">George Tenet</a> ordered the agency to withhold information about <a href="/wiki/Nawaf_al-Hazmi" title="Nawaf al-Hazmi">Nawaf al-Hazmi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khalid_al-Mihdhar" title="Khalid al-Mihdhar">Khalid al-Mihdhar</a> from the rest of the government in an effort to cover up the agency\'s recruitment of the two. George Tenet released a statement denying the agency deliberately withheld information about the pair and noted Clarke himself said he had no proof.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Motives">Motives</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pax_Americana">Pax Americana</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pax_Americana" title="Pax Americana">Pax Americana</a></div>
<p>In September 2000 the <a href="/wiki/Project_for_a_New_American_Century" class="mw-redirect" title="Project for a New American Century">Project for a New American Century</a> (PNAC) released a strategic treatise entitled <i>Rebuilding America\'s Defences</i>. The Defense Planning Guidance of 1992, was drafted by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Wolfowitz" title="Paul Wolfowitz">Paul Wolfowitz</a> on behalf of then <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense" title="United States Secretary of Defense">Secretary of Defense</a> <a href="/wiki/Dick_Cheney" title="Dick Cheney">Dick Cheney</a>. This was described as "a blueprint for permanent American global <a href="/wiki/Hegemony" title="Hegemony">hegemony</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Bacevich" title="Andrew Bacevich">Andrew Bacevich</a> in his book <i>American Empire: The Realities and Consequences of U.S. Diplomacy</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Matt Taibbi argued in his book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Derangement:_A_Terrifying_True_Story_of_War,_Politics,_and_Religion_at_the_Twilight_of_the_American_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="The Great Derangement: A Terrifying True Story of War, Politics, and Religion at the Twilight of the American Empire">The Great Derangement</a></i> that conspiracy theorists have taken what is written in the paper "completely out of context", and that the "transformation" referenced in the paper is explicitly said to be a decades-long process to turn the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>-era military into a "new, modern military" which could deal with more localized conflicts.<sup id="cite_ref-tgd_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tgd-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> He said that, for this to be evidence of motive, either those responsible would have decided to openly state their objectives, or would have read the paper in 2000 and quickly laid the groundwork for the 9/11 attacks using it as inspiration.<sup id="cite_ref-tgd_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tgd-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Invasions">Invasions</span></h3>
<p>Conspiracy theorists have questioned whether <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oil_Factor" title="The Oil Factor">The Oil Factor</a></i> and 9/11 provided the United States and the United Kingdom with a reason to launch a war they had wanted for some time, and suggest that this gives them a strong motive for either carrying out the attacks, or allowing them to take place. For instance, <a href="/wiki/Andreas_von_B%C3%BClow" title="Andreas von B\xc3\xbclow">Andreas von B\xc3\xbclow</a>, a former research minister in the German government, has argued that 9/11 was staged to justify the subsequent wars in Afghanistan and Iraq.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Former Malaysian prime minister <a href="/wiki/Mahathir_Mohamad" title="Mahathir Mohamad">Mahathir Mohamad</a> was quoted as saying that there was "strong evidence" that the attacks were faked so that the United States could go to war against Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> In spite of these allegations, the Bush administration specifically rejected proposals to immediately attack Iraq in response to 9/11,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> and acknowledged that there was no evidence of Iraqi involvement in the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_World_Order">New World Order</span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/New_World_Order_(conspiracy_theory)" title="New World Order (conspiracy theory)">New World Order (conspiracy theory)</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Alex_Jones" title="Alex Jones">Alex Jones</a> and other personalities hold that 9/11 was initiated by a disparate variety of banking, corporate, globalization, and military interests for the purpose of creating a globalist government. Such <a href="/wiki/New_World_Order_conspiracy_theories" class="mw-redirect" title="New World Order conspiracy theories">New World Order conspiracy theories</a> predate 9/11.<sup id="cite_ref-Stahl_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stahl-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Suggested_historical_precedents">Suggested historical precedents</span></h2>
<p>Conspiracy theorists often point to <a href="/wiki/Operation_Northwoods" title="Operation Northwoods">Operation Northwoods</a> as a model for the 9/11 attacks, theorizing the attacks were carried out by the U.S. government as a <a href="/wiki/False_flag" title="False flag">false flag</a> operation and then blamed on Islamic extremists.<sup id="cite_ref-Knight_11-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Knight-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> Operation Northwoods was an unimplemented, apparently rejected, plan approved by the United States Joint Chiefs of Staff in 1962. One proposal in the plan suggested that covert operatives commit multiple acts of terrorism in U.S. cities and blame Cuba, thus providing a pretext for invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)"><i>Time</i></a> magazine contrasted events which inspired past conspiracy theories with those that inspire 9/11 conspiracy theories such as the <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories" title="John F. Kennedy assassination conspiracy theories">assassination of John F. Kennedy</a>. <i>Time</i> called the public assassination of Kennedy a "private, intimate affair" when compared with the attack on the World Trade Center, which was witnessed by millions of people and documented by hundreds of videographers; and said, "there is no event so plain and clear that a determined human being can\'t find ambiguity in it."<sup id="cite_ref-time_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-time-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Proponents">Proponents</span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/9/11_Truth_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11 Truth movement">9/11 Truth movement</a></div>
<p>Many individuals and organizations that support or discuss 9/11 conspiracy theories consider themselves to be part of the 9/11 Truth movement.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Alex_Jones_NY.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/41/Alex_Jones_NY.jpg" decoding="async" width="212" height="219" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="212" data-file-height="219" /></a><figcaption>Alex Jones at a <a href="/wiki/9/11_Truth_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11 Truth Movement">9/11 Truth Movement</a> event in 2007</figcaption></figure>
<p>Prominent adherents of the movement include, among others, radio talk show host <a href="/wiki/Alex_Jones" title="Alex Jones">Alex Jones</a>, former president <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, theologian <a href="/wiki/David_Ray_Griffin" title="David Ray Griffin">David Ray Griffin</a>, physicist <a href="/wiki/Steven_E._Jones" title="Steven E. Jones">Steven E. Jones</a>, software engineer <a href="/wiki/Jim_Hoffman" title="Jim Hoffman">Jim Hoffman</a>, architect Richard Gage (of <a href="/wiki/Architects_%26_Engineers_for_9/11_Truth" title="Architects &amp; Engineers for 9/11 Truth">Architects &amp; Engineers for 9/11 Truth</a>), film producer <a href="/wiki/Dylan_Avery" class="mw-redirect" title="Dylan Avery">Dylan Avery</a>, former Governor of Minnesota <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Ventura" title="Jesse Ventura">Jesse Ventura</a>, former member of the U.S. House of Representatives <a href="/wiki/Cynthia_McKinney" title="Cynthia McKinney">Cynthia McKinney</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Roff_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Roff-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> actors <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Sunjata" title="Daniel Sunjata">Daniel Sunjata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Asner" title="Ed Asner">Ed Asner</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Sheen" title="Charlie Sheen">Charlie Sheen</a>, political science professor Joseph Diaferia and journalist <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Meyssan" title="Thierry Meyssan">Thierry Meyssan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Powell&#124;2006_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Powell|2006-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Manjoo_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manjoo-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CBC-Speculation_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBC-Speculation-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Adherents of the 9/11 Truth movement come from diverse social backgrounds.<sup id="cite_ref-Feuer_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feuer-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Harvey_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harvey-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Curiel_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curiel-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> The movement draws adherents from people of diverse political beliefs including liberals, conservatives, and libertarians.<sup id="cite_ref-Mol\xc3\xa9&#124;2006_76-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mol\xc3\xa9|2006-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Curiel_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curiel-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Barber_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barber-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">Anti-Defamation League</a> has named <a href="/wiki/Alan_Sabrosky" title="Alan Sabrosky">Alan Sabrosky</a> as a key figure in <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">anti-Semitic</a> 9/11 conspiracy theories.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Among the organizations that actively discuss and promote such theories are Architects &amp; Engineers for 9/11 Truth, a group that focuses on the collapse of the World Trade Center buildings; <a href="/wiki/9/11_Truth_movement#9/11_Truth" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11 Truth movement">9/11 Truth</a>, founded in 2004; <a href="/wiki/Scholars_for_9/11_Truth" class="mw-redirect" title="Scholars for 9/11 Truth">Scholars for 9/11 Truth</a>, founded in 2005, and <a href="/wiki/9/11_Truth_movement#Scholars_for_9/11_Truth_&amp;_Justice" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11 Truth movement">Scholars for 9/11 Truth &amp; Justice</a>, a group that split from Scholars for 9/11 Truth in 2007 and runs the online publication <i>Journal of 9/11 Studies</i>; <a href="/wiki/9/11_Citizens_Watch" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11 Citizens Watch">9/11 Citizens Watch</a>, which was already formed in 2002; and the <a href="/wiki/William_Rodriguez" title="William Rodriguez">Hispanic Victims Group</a>. Several of these groups have collected signatures on petitions asking for further investigation of the September 11 attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-ArchitectsEngineers_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArchitectsEngineers-197">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, <a href="/wiki/John_Buchanan_(American_politician)" title="John Buchanan (American politician)">John Buchanan</a> ran for president on a "9/11 Truth" platform.<sup id="cite_ref-upi_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upi-200">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>9/11 Conspiracy theory critic <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Kay" title="Jonathan Kay">Jonathan Kay</a> asserts that for the most part proponents are not out for financial gain and in some cases have left lucrative careers to become activists.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Dr Michael Wood and Dr Karen Douglas <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kent" title="University of Kent">University of Kent</a> psychologists who specialize in conspiracy theories<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> examined the comments sections of over 2000 news articles relating to the collapse of World Trade Center 7. They found that proponents of 9/11 conspiracy theories were more likely to try and debunk the mainstream account than promote their own theories and also were more likely to believe in other conspiracy theories. Proponents of the mainstream account tended to argue for that account and showed a greater hostility toward conspiracy theory proponents.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis">Analysis</span></h3>
<p>According to a 2011 analysis in a <i><a href="/wiki/Skeptical_Inquirer" title="Skeptical Inquirer">Skeptical Inquirer</a></i> article, people involved in this movement, which seemingly is a disparate group with very diversified backgrounds, could be classified into three groups. They join the movement for different reasons, loosely self-assemble to fill different roles and are united by their shared mistrust in experts and the establishment (government and reputable sources of knowledge), and conspiratorial stance. Through their engagement, they each find their own fulfillment and satisfaction. Together, they contribute to the persistence, resilience and exaggerated claims of acceptance (in general public) of the movement. These three groups are:<sup id="cite_ref-Bartlett_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bartlett-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Hard core: The organizers and active members of the various 9/11 Truth Movement organizations. They produce the information, spot the anomalies and technical inconsistencies, provide the technical base and form the theories. While they claim to be only interested in facts and to use <a href="/wiki/Scientific_method" title="Scientific method">scientific method</a>, they commit the logical fallacy of \'<a href="/wiki/Confirmation_bias" title="Confirmation bias">confirmation bias</a>\' by pre-determining the outcome, then searching for corroborating evidence while ignoring the vast body of <a href="/wiki/Peer-review" class="mw-redirect" title="Peer-review">peer-reviewed</a>, independent, consensual research which contradict their theories. They supply the physical structure of the movement by organizing events, seminars, discussions, marches and distributing flyers and pamphlets. Their numbers are relatively small but they are tight-knit and highly connected. Their worldview favors \'super-conspiracy\', a master plan that is behind conspiracies which they believe they are uncovering.<sup id="cite_ref-Bartlett_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bartlett-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Critically turned: They are the young students and political activists whose affiliation with the 9/11 Truth Movement often is rooted from their dissatisfaction and anger at the established political and social order. Their sense of justice and <a href="/wiki/Idealism" title="Idealism">idealism</a> propels them to activism against perceived oppression and social injustice. Their penchant to use Internet, especially <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">social media</a>, and tech savvy make them the propaganda machine for the movement. They produce <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> videos and films with cool, countercultural content, make good use of pop culture parody and eye-catching graphics. The countercultural street cred of their productions buy them broad appeal and exposure to millions of people.<sup id="cite_ref-Bartlett_204-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bartlett-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Illiterati: They are the movement\'s mass membership backbone, a large, diffuse group which give the movement exaggerated claims of popularity and influence. Participation in the 9/11 Truth Movement, to this group of people, is as much a social and recreational pursuit as the quest for truth. Their partaking is mostly through <a href="/wiki/Web_2.0" title="Web 2.0">web 2.0</a> social networking and YouTube. Their commentaries often are emotional and they make no pretense to be accurate, balanced or to show genuine intent to find truth. Involvement with the movement that fit their worldview gives them a sense of identity and belonging, which they find more appealing than the facts and evidences of the 9/11 terrorist attack itself.<sup id="cite_ref-Bartlett_204-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bartlett-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_reaction">Media reaction</span></h2>
<p>While discussion and coverage of these theories is mainly confined to Internet pages, books, documentary films, and conversation, a number of mainstream news outlets around the world have covered the issue.
</p><p>The Norwegian version of the July 2006 <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde_diplomatique" title="Le Monde diplomatique">Le Monde diplomatique</a></i> sparked interest when they ran, on their own initiative, a three-page main story on the 9/11 attacks and summarized the various types of 9/11 conspiracy theories (which were not specifically endorsed by the newspaper, only recensed).<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> In December 2006, the French version published an article by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Cockburn" title="Alexander Cockburn">Alexander Cockburn</a>, co-editor of <i><a href="/wiki/CounterPunch" title="CounterPunch">CounterPunch</a></i>, which strongly criticized the alleged endorsement of conspiracy theories by the U.S. left-wing, alleging that it was a sign of "theoretical emptiness."<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Also, on the Canadian website for <i>CBC News: <a href="/wiki/The_Fifth_Estate_(TV)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Fifth Estate (TV)">The Fifth Estate</a></i>, a program titled, "Conspiracy Theories: uncovering the facts behind the myths of Sept. 11, 2001" was broadcast on October 29, 2003, stating that what they found may be more surprising than any theories.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> On November 27, 2009, <i>The Fifth Estate</i> aired a documentary entitled <i>The Unofficial Story</i> where several prominent members of the 9/11 Truth Movement made their case.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>An article in the September 11, 2006, edition of <i>Time</i> magazine comments that the major 9/11 conspiracy theories "depend on circumstantial evidence, facts without analysis or documentation, quotes taken out of context and the scattered testimony of traumatized eyewitnesses", and enjoy continued popularity because "the idea that there is a malevolent controlling force orchestrating global events is, in a perverse way, comforting". It concludes that "conspiracy theories are part of the process by which Americans deal with traumatic public events" and constitute "an American form of national mourning."<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Australian newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph_(Sydney)" title="The Daily Telegraph (Sydney)">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> published an article titled "The CIA couldn\'t have organised this&#160;..." which said "The same people who are making a mess of Iraq were never so clever or devious that they could stage a complex assault on two narrow towers of steel and glass" and "if there is a nefarious plot in all this bad planning, it is one improvised by a confederacy of dunces". This article mainly attacked a group of scientists led by Professor <a href="/wiki/Steven_E._Jones" title="Steven E. Jones">Steven E. Jones</a>, now called <a href="/wiki/9/11_Truth_Movement#Scholars_for_9/11_Truth_&amp;_Justice" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11 Truth Movement">Scholars for 9/11 Truth and Justice</a>. They said "most of them aren\'t scientists but instructors&#160;... at second-rate colleges".<sup id="cite_ref-CIACouldntHaveOrganisedThis_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIACouldntHaveOrganisedThis-211">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>The Daily Telegraph</i> also published an article in May 2007 that was highly critical of <i>Loose Change 2</i>, a movie which presents a 9/11 conspiracy theory.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Doug MacEachern in a May 2008 column for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Arizona_Republic" title="The Arizona Republic">The Arizona Republic</a></i> wrote that while many "9/11 truthers" are not crackpots that espouse "crackpot conspiracy theories", supporters of the theories fail to take into account both human nature and that nobody has come forward claiming they were participants in the alleged conspiracies.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> This view was seconded by Timothy Giannuzzi, a <i><a href="/wiki/Calgary_Herald" title="Calgary Herald">Calgary Herald</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Op-ed" title="Op-ed">op-ed</a> columnist specializing in foreign policy.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 7, 2008, the <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i> published a lengthy article on the <a href="/wiki/9/11_Truth_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11 Truth Movement">9/11 Truth Movement</a> and 9/11 conspiracy theories.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Charlie_Brooker" title="Charlie Brooker">Charlie Brooker</a>, a British comedian and multimedia personality, in a July 2008 column published by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> as part of its "Comment is free" series agreed that 9/11 conspiracy theorists fail to take in account human fallacies and added that believing in these theories gives theorists a sense of belonging to a community that shares privileged information thus giving the theorists a delusional sense of power.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> The commentary generated over 1700 online responses, the largest in the history of the series.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> In a September 2009 piece, <i>The Guardian</i> was more supportive of 9/11 conspiracy theories, asking, "when did it become uncool to ask questions? When did questioners become imbeciles?"<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 12, 2008, <a href="/wiki/All-Russia_State_Television_and_Radio_Broadcasting_Company" title="All-Russia State Television and Radio Broadcasting Company">Russian State Television</a> broadcast in prime time a documentary made by <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">Member of the European Parliament</a> <a href="/wiki/Giulietto_Chiesa" title="Giulietto Chiesa">Giulietto Chiesa</a> entitled <i>Zero</i>, sympathetic to those who question the accepted account of the attacks according to Chiesa. According to <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Meyssan" title="Thierry Meyssan">Thierry Meyssan</a> in conjunction with the documentary, Russian State Television aired a debate on the subject. The panel consisted of members from several countries including 12 Russians who hold divergent views. The motive of Russian State Television in broadcasting the documentary was questioned by a commentator from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Other_Russia_(coalition)" title="The Other Russia (coalition)">The Other Russia</a></i> who noted that Russian State Television had a history of broadcasting programs involving <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theory" title="Conspiracy theory">conspiracy theories</a> involving the <a href="/wiki/United_States_government" class="mw-redirect" title="United States government">United States government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nasir Mahmood in a commentary printed by the <i><a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Observer" title="Pakistan Observer">Pakistan Observer</a></i> wrote favorably about a 9/11 truth lecture and film festival held in California and quoted a Jewish speaker at that festival who said that none of the 19 suspected hijackers had been proven guilty of anything and compared racism against Muslims resulting from what he called false accusations to the racism against Jews in the Nazi era.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 10, 2008, <a href="/wiki/ITN" title="ITN">ITN</a> broadcast a story summarizing various 9/11 conspiracy theories.<sup id="cite_ref-ITN081110_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ITN081110-221">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The emergence of the <a href="/wiki/Birther_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Birther movement">birther movement</a> in 2009 has led to comparisons between that movement and the 9/11 Truth movement, with both movements seen in a very negative light. <a href="/wiki/Moon_landing_conspiracy_theories" title="Moon landing conspiracy theories">Moon landing conspiracy theories</a> have also been compared to the birther and 9/11 conspiracy theories. James Borne, a journalist for <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> who covered the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>, described his assignment covering a 9/11 truth meeting as "[p]erhaps the most intellectually scary assignment I have had in recent years".<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 31, 2009, the <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Channel" class="mw-redirect" title="National Geographic Channel">National Geographic Channel</a> aired the program <i>9/11 Science and Conspiracy</i>, in which the <a href="/wiki/Energetic_Materials_Research_and_Testing_Center" title="Energetic Materials Research and Testing Center">Energetic Materials Research and Testing Center</a> tested some of the claims frequently made by those who question the accepted 9/11 account. Specifically, the experiments concluded that burning jet fuel alone can sufficiently raise the temperature of a steel support column to the point of structural failure, that a controlled demolition using conventional techniques would leave clear evidence that was not found at Ground Zero, that using <a href="/wiki/Thermite" title="Thermite">thermite</a> is not an effective technique to melt a steel column, and that even if thermite chemical signatures were found, it would be impossible to tell if thermite was actually used or if the traces came from the reaction of aircraft aluminum with other substances in the fire. The testing also concluded that the type of hole found at the Pentagon was consistent with the standard scenario, and that damage from a bombing or missile attack would differ from the damage that occurred. In the program, several prominent 9/11 conspiracy theorists viewed rough edits of the experiments, and expressed their disagreement with the findings.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The British left wing magazine <i><a href="/wiki/New_Statesman" title="New Statesman">New Statesman</a></i> listed <a href="/wiki/David_Ray_Griffin" title="David Ray Griffin">David Ray Griffin</a> as the 41st most important person who matters today. The magazine said that Griffin\'s "books on the subject have lent a sheen of respectability that appeals to people at the highest levels of government". The publication listed 9/11 conspiracy theories as "one of the most pernicious global myths".<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Griffin\'s book <i>The New Pearl Harbor Revisited</i> was chosen by Publishers Weekly as a "Pick of the Week" in November 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Denver <a href="/wiki/Public_television" class="mw-redirect" title="Public television">public television</a> <a href="/wiki/KBDI-TV" title="KBDI-TV">KBDI-TV</a> has aired 9/11 truth documentaries several times. The stations spokesperson claimed airing these documentaries has been a boon for the stations fund raising efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Glenn_Beck" title="Glenn Beck">Glenn Beck</a>, television and radio host, said of the allegations: "There are limits to debasement of this country, aren\'t there? I mean, it\'s one thing to believe that our politicians are capable of being <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Madoff" title="Bernie Madoff">Bernie Madoff</a>. It\'s another to think that they are willing to kill 3,000 Americans. Once you cross that line, you\'re in a whole new territory."<sup id="cite_ref-WSJ_Watching_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJ_Watching-231">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2010, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> editorialized against <a href="/wiki/Yukihisa_Fujita" title="Yukihisa Fujita">Yukihisa Fujita</a>, a prominent Japanese politician who has espoused 9/11 conspiracy theories. They described Fujita as a man "susceptible to the imaginings of the lunatic fringe". It went on to say that the <a href="/wiki/Japan%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Japan\xe2\x80\x93United States relations">U.S.\xe2\x80\x93Japan alliance</a> would be "severely tested" if Fujita\'s party continued to tolerate these kinds of comments.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For the ninth anniversary of the attacks the Egyptian daily <i><a href="/wiki/Al-masry_Al-youm" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-masry Al-youm">Al-masry Al-youm</a></i> published an article questioning the U.S. Government story and promoting conspiracy theories. The senior analyst for the semi-official <a href="/wiki/Al-Ahram_Center_for_Political_and_Strategic_Studies" title="Al-Ahram Center for Political and Strategic Studies">Al-Ahram Center for Political and Strategic Studies</a> and a member of Parliament from the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood" title="Muslim Brotherhood">Muslim Brotherhood</a> was quoted.
</p><p>Gordon Farrer, the technology editor for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Age" title="The Age">The Age</a></i>, theorized in a November 2010 column for the <i><a href="/wiki/Sydney_Morning_Herald" class="mw-redirect" title="Sydney Morning Herald">Sydney Morning Herald</a></i> that the popularity of 9/11 conspiracy theories was a result of two main factors. One revolved around the personality traits of the theorists themselves (cynical, anxious, belief that they are <a href="/wiki/Freethought" title="Freethought">freethinkers</a>). The second revolved around the high <a href="/wiki/Internet_search" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet search">internet search</a> ranking 9/11 conspiracy theories receive, leading to a false air of authority to the theories. Speaking of the theorists. Farrer wrote that "when politicians and media don\'t give them voice they feel more threatened, more suspicious, cornered, helpless; and so they go on the attack".<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Geraldo_Rivera" title="Geraldo Rivera">Geraldo Rivera</a>, the host of <i><a href="/wiki/Geraldo_at_Large" title="Geraldo at Large">Geraldo at Large</a></i>, a news magazine run by <a href="/wiki/Fox_News_Channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Fox News Channel">Fox News Channel</a>, expressed openness to questions on causes of the collapse of <a href="/wiki/7_World_Trade_Center" title="7 World Trade Center">7 World Trade Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fox_takes_heat_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox_takes_heat-234">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Napolitano" title="Andrew Napolitano">Andrew Napolitano</a>, a legal analyst for Fox News and former judge at the <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Superior_Court" title="New Jersey Superior Court">New Jersey Superior Court</a>, voiced support for skepticism about the collapse of the high-rise building, and for Rivera investigating the event.<sup id="cite_ref-Fox_takes_heat_234-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fox_takes_heat-234">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Alex Jones syndicated radio program was dropped by 70 radio stations when he began espousing 9/11 conspiracy theories.<sup id="cite_ref-StrangeMan_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StrangeMan-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> On August 29, 2010, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two" title="BBC Two">BBC Two</a> broadcast a program entitled <i>The Conspiracy Files: 9/11 \xe2\x80\x93 Ten Years On</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCMag_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCMag-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 5, 2011, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> published an article entitled, "9/11 conspiracy theories debunked". The article noted that unlike the collapse of World Trade Centers 1 and 2 a controlled demolition collapses a building from the bottom and explains that the windows popped because of collapsing floors. The article also said there are conspiracy theories that claim that <a href="/wiki/7_World_Trade_Center" title="7 World Trade Center">7 World Trade Center</a> was also downed by a controlled demolition, that the Pentagon being hit by a missile, that the hijacked planes were packed with explosives and flown by remote control, that Israel was behind the attacks, that a plane headed for the Pentagon was shot down by a missile, that there was <a href="/wiki/Insider_trading" title="Insider trading">insider trading</a> by people who had foreknowledge of the attacks were all false.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Toure_Neblett" class="mw-redirect" title="Toure Neblett">Toure Neblett</a>, who has Tweeted his suspicions about the attack on the Pentagon, is one of the hosts of the <a href="/wiki/MSNBC" title="MSNBC">MSNBC</a> program <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cycle_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Cycle (TV series)">The Cycle</a></i>, which debuted on June 25, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span></h2>
<p>Critics of these conspiracy theories say they are a form of <a href="/wiki/Conspiracism" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspiracism">conspiracism</a> common throughout history after a traumatic event in which <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theory" title="Conspiracy theory">conspiracy theories</a> emerge as a mythic form of explanation.<sup id="cite_ref-Barkun&#124;2003_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barkun|2003-238">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> A related criticism addresses the form of research on which the theories are based. Thomas W. Eagar, an engineering professor at <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a>, suggested they "use the \'reverse scientific method\'. They determine what happened, throw out all the data that doesn\'t fit their conclusion, and then hail their findings as the only possible conclusion." Eagar\'s criticisms also exemplify a common stance that the theories are best ignored. "I\'ve told people that if the argument gets too mainstream, I\'ll engage in the debate." According to him, this happened when Steve Jones, a physics professor at <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young_University" title="Brigham Young University">Brigham Young University</a>, took up the issue.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Michael_Shermer" title="Michael Shermer">Michael Shermer</a>, writing in <i><a href="/wiki/Scientific_American" title="Scientific American">Scientific American</a></i>, said:
"The mistaken belief that a handful of unexplained anomalies can undermine a well-established theory lies at the heart of all conspiratorial thinking. All the evidence for a 9/11 conspiracy falls under the rubric of this fallacy. Such notions are easily refuted by noting that scientific theories are not built on single facts alone but on a convergence of evidence assembled from multiple lines of inquiry."<sup id="cite_ref-SciAm_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SciAm-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Scientific_American" title="Scientific American">Scientific American</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-SciAm_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SciAm-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Popular_Mechanics" title="Popular Mechanics">Popular Mechanics</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Skeptic%27s_Dictionary" title="The Skeptic&#39;s Dictionary">The Skeptic\'s Dictionary</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> have published articles that rebut various 9/11 conspiracy theories. <i>Popular Mechanics</i> has published a book entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Debunking_9/11_Myths" title="Debunking 9/11 Myths">Debunking 9/11 Myths</a></i> that expands upon the research first presented in the article.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> In the foreword for the book <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">Senator</a> <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a> wrote that blaming the U.S. government for the events "mars the memories of all those lost on that day" and "exploits the public\'s anger and sadness. It shakes Americans\' faith in their government at a time when that faith is already near an all-time low. It trafficks in ugly, unfounded accusations of extraordinary evil against fellow Americans."<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Spiegel" title="Der Spiegel">Der Spiegel</a></i> dismissed 9/11 conspiracy theories as a "panoply of the absurd", stating "as diverse as these theories and their adherents may be, they share a basic thought pattern: great tragedies must have great reasons."<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Journalist <a href="/wiki/Matt_Taibbi" title="Matt Taibbi">Matt Taibbi</a>, in his book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Great_Derangement:_A_Terrifying_True_Story_of_War,_Politics,_and_Religion_at_the_Twilight_of_the_American_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="The Great Derangement: A Terrifying True Story of War, Politics, and Religion at the Twilight of the American Empire">The Great Derangement</a></i>, discusses 9/11 conspiracy theories as symptomatic of what he calls the "derangement" of American society; a disconnection from reality due to widespread "disgust with our political system".<sup id="cite_ref-tgd_180-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tgd-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Drawing a parallel with the <a href="/wiki/Charismatic_Movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Charismatic Movement">Charismatic Movement</a>, he argues that both "chose to battle bugbears that were completely idiotic, fanciful, and imaginary," instead of taking control of their own lives.<sup id="cite_ref-tgd_180-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tgd-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> While critical, Taibbi explains that 9/11 conspiracy theories are different from "<a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Clinton</a>-era <a href="/wiki/Black_helicopter" title="Black helicopter">black-helicopter paranoia</a>", and constitute more than "a small, scattered group of nutcases [...] they really were, just as they claim to be, almost everyone you meet."<sup id="cite_ref-tgd_180-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tgd-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/David_Aaronovitch" title="David Aaronovitch">David Aaronovitch</a>, a columnist for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>, in his book entitled <i>Voodoo Histories: The Role of the Conspiracy Theory in Shaping Modern History</i> that was published in May 2009, claimed that the theories strain credulity.<sup id="cite_ref-women.timesonline.co.uk_77-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-women.timesonline.co.uk-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> He charges that 9/11 conspiracy theorists have exaggerated the expertise of those supporting their theories, and says 9/11 conspiracy theorists, including <a href="/wiki/David_Ray_Griffin" title="David Ray Griffin">David Ray Griffin</a>, cross-cite each other.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> He also claims the popularity of 9/11 conspiracy theories has hurt the <a href="/wiki/War_on_Terror" class="mw-redirect" title="War on Terror">War on Terror</a>. According to Aaronovitch, because a significant portion of educated Pakistanis believe that <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> brought the towers down, dealing with the <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> is difficult "because they actually don\'t believe the fundamental premise on which the war against terror was waged".<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a> law professor <a href="/wiki/Cass_Sunstein" title="Cass Sunstein">Cass Sunstein</a> co-authored a 2009 paper which used members of the 9/11 Truth movement and others as examples of people who suffer from "crippled epistemologies", to public trust and the political system. He wrote that "[t]hey do not merely undermine democratic debate&#160;[...] In extreme cases, they create or fuel violence. If government can dispel such theories, it should do so."<sup id="cite_ref-StrangeMan_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StrangeMan-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Institute_of_British_Architects" title="Royal Institute of British Architects">Royal Institute of British Architects</a> (RIBA) was criticized for hosting a lecture by Richard Gage, president of Architects &amp; Engineers for 9/11 Truth. Rick Bell, the director of the <a href="/wiki/American_Institute_of_Architects" title="American Institute of Architects">American Institute of Architects</a> (AIA) New York chapter, who was a witness to the 9/11 attacks, said that "no amount of money" would persuade him to allow the group to talk at his headquarters and said that Gage lacks credibility among the professional community. <a href="/wiki/Kohn_Pedersen_Fox" title="Kohn Pedersen Fox">Eugine Kohn</a>, former spokesperson for the AIA, said Gage\'s theories were "ridiculous", "[t]here were no explosives planted", and "[t]he buildings were definitely brought down by the planes". The decision to host the event was also criticized by the former president of RIBA and the founding president of the AIA\'s United Kingdom chapter. Gage has been warned by the AIA against giving a false impression that he has a relationship with it. A July 2012 article in the AIA\'s magazine criticized Gage for continuing to intimate that he has an association with the organization, and claimed that there were no architects at an Architects and Engineers for 9/11 Truth screening held in an AIA boardroom.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> RIBA released a statement saying the perception that it endorses events held in its buildings is "regrettable", and said it would review policy on "private hire" of its buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> Anthony Summers and Robbyn Swan offer scathing criticism of many of the above theories in <i>The Eleventh Day</i>, their 2011 investigation of the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>U.S. representative <a href="/wiki/Peter_T._King" class="mw-redirect" title="Peter T. King">Peter T. King</a>, chairmen of the <a href="/wiki/House_Homeland_Security_Committee" class="mw-redirect" title="House Homeland Security Committee">House Homeland Security Committee</a>, said 9/11 conspiracy theorists "trivialize" the "most tragic event to affect the United States" and that "[p]eople making these claims are disgraceful, and they should be ashamed of themselves".<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The hosts of "<a href="/wiki/The_Skeptics%27_Guide_to_the_Universe" title="The Skeptics&#39; Guide to the Universe">The Skeptics\' Guide to the Universe</a>" (the "SGU") have spoken repeatedly about the "absurdity of 9/11 conspiracy theories". In addition to critiquing the theories using the same or similar arguments as the above, the "SGU" hosts say that, like most conspiracy theories, this one collapses under its own weight and contradicts itself. In order for the 9/11 conspiracy theories to be correct, the U.S. government would not only have to orchestrate the claimed false flag operation regarding the airplanes that crashed into the World Trade Center, but they would also have to orchestrate a superfluous controlled demolition and cover their tracks so flawlessly that it becomes indistinguishable to physicists from the "official story", yet the plan would have to be flawed enough so that "losers in their mothers\' basement" will discover the conspiracy.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_politics">In politics</span></h2>
<p>Former Canadian <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Canada" title="Liberal Party of Canada">Liberal Party</a> leader <a href="/wiki/St%C3%A9phane_Dion" title="St\xc3\xa9phane Dion">St\xc3\xa9phane Dion</a> forced a candidate from <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg" title="Winnipeg">Winnipeg</a>, Lesley Hughes, to terminate her campaign after earlier writings from Hughes surfaced in which Hughes wrote that U.S., German, Russian and Israeli intelligence officials knew about the 9/11 attacks in advance.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BeWaryOfThoseWhoSay911WasAFake_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BeWaryOfThoseWhoSay911WasAFake-254">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Kent" title="Peter Kent">Peter Kent</a>, Deputy Editor of <a href="/wiki/Global_Television_Network" title="Global Television Network">Global Television Network</a> News and a <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_of_Canada" title="Conservative Party of Canada">Conservative Party</a> candidate in the 2008 Canadian election, had earlier called for Hughes\'s resignation, saying that the 9/11 Truth movement is "one of Canada\'s most notorious hatemongering fringe movements" composed of "conspiracy theorists who are notorious for holding anti-Semitic views."<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> On June 16, 2009, Hughes sued Kent, the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Jewish_Congress" title="Canadian Jewish Congress">Canadian Jewish Congress</a>, the <a href="/wiki/B%27nai_B%27rith" title="B&#39;nai B&#39;rith">B\'nai B\'rith</a> of Canada and four senior members of the two organizations, alleging the <a href="/wiki/Antisemitic" class="mw-redirect" title="Antisemitic">antisemitic</a> allegations were untrue and defamatory and ruined her career.<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> Later, another Conservative Party candidate called for the leader of the <a href="/wiki/New_Democratic_Party_of_Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="New Democratic Party of Canada">New Democratic Party</a> to fire a candidate for her pro-9/11 truth views.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Zijad_Delic" class="mw-redirect" title="Zijad Delic">Zijad Delic</a>, head of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Islamic_Congress" title="Canadian Islamic Congress">Canadian Islamic Congress</a>, Canada\'s largest Muslim advocacy organization, is trying to remove 9/11 conspiracy theorists from its board, in an effort to what he describes as purifying within and totally canadianize the organization.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, calls for the resignation of <a href="/wiki/Richard_Falk" class="mw-redirect" title="Richard Falk">Richard Falk</a>, the special rapporteur on human rights in the Palestinian territories for the United Nations, were partially based on his support investigating the validity of 9/11 conspiracy theories.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Falk praised a book by David Ray Griffin. Falk was condemned for his remarks by <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretary_General" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Secretary General">United Nations Secretary General</a> <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> and United States ambassador to the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Susan_Rice" title="Susan Rice">Susan Rice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup>
